# Adventures in Glorantha — OCR Extraction

> **WARNING**: This file contains severely garbled text due to the source PDF's non-standard
> font encoding. The text is largely unreadable. Use `cultures-mistral.json` for structured
> culture data, and `creation-summary-aig.json` for character creation steps.
> The garbling is in the PDF's text layer, not an OCR failure — pdfplumber produces
> identical garbled output. The PDF (200MB) also exceeds vision-mode size limits.

PAMALTELA

### Page 31
& a
Pure Brithini and God Forgotten meet, special interpreters
are required because the Brithini refuse to sully their mouths
with the atrocity the God Forgotten have developed.

Macic

Like the Buthini, the God Forgotten are masters of sor-
cery, the predominant higher magic of Western culture,
practised extensively and exclusively by the Zzistori. As gods
are not worshipped, Rune Magic is unavailable to them,
and Spitit Magic is viewed as a curious and pointless dab-
bling with lesser creatures that cannot be bothered taking
corporeal form. Folk Magic is considered to be a natural and
much diluted form of sorcery and so is practiced widely by
all castes.

LUNAR HEARTLAND CULTURE

"Tam Essuira the Grave, a citiem of Glamour and proud servant
of the Red Emperor Now you are here, you wll soon find that We Are
ANUS."

This is the culture found in the heartlands of the Lunar
Empire, with origins in the solar empire of Dara Happa.
The Solar civilization of the Pelorian basin is a proud and
ancient culture; in the Gods Age, they were ruled by Yelm
andhis son Murharzarm, the first Emperor of Dara Happa.
At the Dawn, they were niled by Pentan horse nomads called
the Sons of the Sun, but the Dara Happan Empire was re-
established in 221. The Pelorian people have been ruled by.
the Red Emperor since 1250, and constitute the heartland of
the mighty Lunar Empire.

Lunar Heartland culture is actually divided into two cul-
tural subtypes. One, confined to the dense cities of the Oslir
River and its tributaries, is Dara Happan, the inheritors of a
proudand ancient heritage. The other, called Lodrilli is less
exalted, Jess pretentious, and is considered by many to be a
watered-down, decentralized version of the Dara Happan
culture. The Dara Happans are the heirs of Yelm’s origi-
nal Solar Empire that lay upon the mighty Oslir River val-
ley at the centre of Peloria. Yelm made the laws and rules
that govern the cities even today. Their Golden Age heritage
has conférred on them marvellous magics and a tradition

GFHominOnCeame vz Od

### Page 32
of urban life that influences the surrounding world. Dara
Happans can be found on both sides of the Oslir River, fiom
‘Jillaro to the Keniryan Sea, as well as ruling isolated cities
throughout the Empire.

Ourside of the Dara Happan cities live the Lodrilli farmer
peoples, who worship Lodril and a host of agricukwral and
fertility deities. These people have lived here since the Dark-
ness, ruled at times by trolls, horse barbarians, Dara Hap-
pans, Camanians and Odlanthi. Even though they are called
“farmer peoples" by the Dara Happans, several Lodrilli sub
types, most notably the Pelandans of the Oronin river valley,
have their own wadition of urban civiisation.

Even though the Dara Happan and Lodtilli traditions dif=
fer in some respects, they are still civilised cultures; for game
purposes, skills are very similar.

Dara Happans consider the City to be the only true way
of life. Yelm built the first cities and chose the first citizens,
theancestor: of all Dara Happans. Trade is considered to be
a special benefit of the Sun God, and Pdorian village lifeis a
source of jokes. City dwellers scorn anyone who lives outside
city walls, even if they live in the valley and arc descendants
of a solar deity

The Lodrilli farmer peoples are mostly content to stay in
their villages, grow rice, maize and barley, and to raise pigs,
goats and catle. They use a simple plough, lite more than
a long, sharpened, fire-hardened stick (blessed by Lodril),
pulled by a pair of oxen. Buildings are typically made of
mud-brick. Most Lodrillj cities are simply big villages whose
foreign populace cventually took contro] from the native
farmers. Whether internal laws are drawn from Carmanian,
Dara Happan, or Theyalan customs, all cities ame indepen-
dent bodies, generally run by a guild council.

‘Lunar Heariland society is extremely stratified and divided
into Nobles, Wimesses and Officers, Headmen, Workers and
Slaves. Atthe very top of this pyramid are the Red Emperor
and his household, who are, considered living deities. The
Witnesses and Officers are the lesser aristocracy of minor
priesthoods, bureaucrats, and officers. Headmen include vik
lage headmen, overseers, artisans, merchants, soldiers, merce-
naries and soon. They are counted as “half-citizens” and are
not allowed to become full Dara Happan citizens. Workers do
most of the actual labour. They are traditionally categorized
into foreman, digger, harvester, labourer, cooper, carpenter,
potter, camier and boss. Slavery is common in Peloria; most
slaves serve as agricultural workers. Slaves are obtained as a

OuUrrttne @8fTAARe BK

31

ADVENTURES IN GLORANTHA 4 CHARACTERS ae

result of wars, rebellions, or the failure of a community or
individual to pay taxes.

Jamar Heartlanders, be they Dara Happan or Lodrilli,
tend to be tall, of regal bearing, stocky of build, and with a
natural elegance that is a direct result of their relationship
with both Yelm and the Red Goddess. Their skin is burnished
to an almost golden hue, and their hair — thick and luxuriant
~is either blond, light brown or flame-red. Eyes are brown or
amber, and the facial bone structure is strong and imposing.
‘The Dara Happan nose isa distinctive feature; welldefined
almost chiselled — and, in certain aristocratic families, hooked
with impressive, flaring nostrils. ‘The eyes are typically heavily
Fdded and slant downwards at the temple. Lips are thin cres-
cents, and the jawhne strong and purposeful, Almost without
exception, Heartlanders are all siriking in their appearance,
fiom the humblest Lodrilli through to the wealthiest Dara
Happan.

Pride is of the greatest importance to Lunar Heartlanders,
especially to Dara Happans, and even the lowliest Lodrilli can
list his family and lineage for many generations, and will do so
at any opportunity when engaging with foreigners. Declaim-
ing lineage in this way asserts natural supremacy over other
peoples, but is never delivered with purposefidl arrogance.
‘Lamar Heartlanders know and understand hurnility, but they
do not care to make it the basis of their nature. With such an
extensive and noble history, they expect to be granted respect,
but do not immediately demandit.

All Heartlanders believe in justice, which is not the same
as freedom or equality. Justice is the Red Emperor's justice,
which means fairness as directed by the Red Goddess and the
Laws of the Empire. This justice includes the concept of hos-
pitality, but precludes charity. A good and just Lunar Heart-
lander is borpitable to anyone who comes to his house or
who seeks help; but hospitality does not automatically grant
entilement. A peasant secking refuuge in the house of a noble
‘will be welcomed butgiven a stable floor to sleep on, bread to
eat and water to drink. It is not the peasant’s right t expect
more, butneither is he expected to accept anything less.

Heartlanders tend not to possess any intrinsic notions of
obligation. It is right arid just to listen to the needs of oth-
ers, but no Lunar Heartlancer, especially a Dara Happan,
ever feels obliged, save by dint of station, to offer help. In
their general outlook they are open, as honest as their station
entitles them to be, and fond of laughter at the right times.
Despite their aloof physical appearance, Lunar Heartlind-
ers are welcoming and good company, but maintain a calm

Geom tn Onreaowme2Vs 0

### Page 33
* ADVENTURES IN GLORANTHA & CHARACTERS

reserve when the situation demands it. They are not prone to
irrational outbursts or violent rages. Anger manifests itself as
a cool rebuke followed by a dignified withdrawal. Happiness
is the abundant use of sly wit, subtle jokesas dry as the des-
ext sands, and a playful chiding that echoes Lodhil’s earthy
humour. Vulgarity and lewdness is disdained, but every
Heartlander harbours bawdy streak that emerges slowly in
the right company and circumstances.
‘LANGUAGE

New Pelorian is the official state language. It has a writ-
ten script adapted from Dara Happan, but far easierto learn
and to write. Many foreigners fear that the Red Goddess”
philosophical insights are embedded in both the spoken and
written forms of New Pelorian.
Macic

‘Lumar Heartlanders have acomplex mythology that, prior
tp the Red Goddess's birth, was centred firmly on the theistic
worship of the Cdestial Emperor Yelm and his many sons,
daughters and associated gods and goddesses. This worship
is still maintained in the Dara Happan cities, where the Solar
Gods provide Miracles through their devout cults. Since the
Red Goddess’s birth, a new religion and a newmagic, ema~
nating from the Red Goddess herself, has arisen which both
complements, but alsothreatens to overshadow, the ald Solar
religion. The magic of the Lunar Empire is entirely unlike
the theism of the old gods, although it has its own pantheon
of god and demigods, exemplified in the cult of the Seven
Mothers. Lunar Magic is tied to the power of the Red God-
dess and waxes and wanes with the Red Moon’s phases Itis
described in its own chapter, starting om page XX.

LUNAR PROVINCIAL CULTURE

"Thep know me as Jervis and I am in the service of Duke Raus of
Rone. Ht gives me pleasure to serve the Reaching Moon at the furthest
edge of its poovex"

While the Lunars of the Empire's Heartlands have their
roots in traditional Dara Happan society, there are citizens
of the Empire who are just as devout, but have grown up"
far removed from the structured and mannered echelons of
motherlands directly beneath the Red Moon. These are the
Provincial Lunars, those who dwell within the Glowline and
quite often beyond it, but have no ties with the old Dara
‘Happan ways and ideals.

Many Lunar Provincials still have ties to the heartlands,
either having left them to take up posts at the Red Emperor’s
decree, or having family in the old country even though they
themselves were born in the Glowline’s outer beams. Thus,
while these provindals have adopted many of the customs
of their current home, a certain Dara Happan mind-set
and sense of entitement remains. Some provincials remain

Fear nOmZxeamevVez00

### Page 34
resolute in maintaining their old identity and customs, delib-
erately dressing and acting in fashions that are culturally idio-
syncratic, attempting, all the while, to establish and protect a
Little Dara Happa, or a Little Glamour or Raibanth, wher-
ever they might be. Others, of course, integrate, leaming the
Jocal language, aflecting|ocal customs and attempting, as best
they can, to get along with the peoples they have conquered.
For many though, the Heardand Ways reniain just that, and
are considered superior in every way to the tried, tested and
established customs of the indigenous habitants.

Lamar Provincials then, frequently display the defining
characteristics of Lamar Heartlanders, but often have some
of the sensibilities of their current home. And, evenif they do
not choose to embrace the culture and customs of their colo-
nial abode, they are well enough versed in what these mean
in relation to traditional Dara Happan and Lodrilli values for
them toempathise with their indigenous neighbours.

Provincial Lynars tend to remain loyal and tue to the
‘ways and lore of the Reaching Moon, but this does notneces-
sarily mean that they are totally loyal and committed to serv-
ing the Red Emperot. Some are resentful at having to serve
so far from home; those who are being actively punished are
likely to be bitter too, Those serving in the Imperial Lunar
Army have little say in where they serve (or, indeed, their loy-
abies), but at the empire's far flung reaches, there is no doubt
they are denied the comforts of life back in the heartland cit-
~ies, Here, they must endure unfamiliar weather, food, hygiene
and other indignities, all the’ while keeping the peace, fighting
those who would break the peace, or finding new peoples who
need to have peace imposed on them.

In short, Provincial Lunars are far from home, sometimes
willingly, more often not; farced into dealing with people
they might otherwise avoid and sometimes being pleasantly
surprised by their experiences. Yet they are still required to
espouse and represent core Lunar values and traditions, often
in areas that despise these things and would happily sec every
last Lunar dead. Provincial Lunars are hardened to life on the
fiontier, wary of the locals, wary of those cheerful Heartland-
ers who came to"visit for a season or two’, yet prepared to try
to make the best of it..

LANGUAGE

New Pelorian, plus Tradetalk and the local language.
Provincial Lunars know that being able to speak some of the
local tongue helps enormously and those bom and raised
in the provinces often learn the local tongue alongside their
mother language.

PRAXIAN CULTURE

"You, challeye me, Ozenth Ionfoot of the Pal Jom? Good! We
meet in the Block's westerly shadow atdawn and I shall show you what

your entrails look like!"

‘The vast area known asthe Wastclands is one of the most
desolate and inhospitable regions of Glorantha, yet it is also
home to one of its oldestand most unique cultures: the ani-
mal riding nomads of Prax. These proud and hardy people
are organised into several tribes, each of which rides and
herds a differenttype of beast, such as sables, impalas, zebras
and rhinos. There are five Great Tribes (Bison, High Llama,
Impala, Sable and Morokanth) and many lesser ones. They
wander across the chaparral and deserts of their territory
secking new grazing lanck, raiding rival tribes, and fighting
outsiders and Chaos. The best lands are found in Prax, and
competitionis fierce over the right to graze there; the weaker
‘tribes often find themselves banished to the harsh environ-
ment of Vultures Country and beyond for several years at
atime.

Life for the Praxians is hard, and they depend on their
beasts for survival, providing them with meat, milk, leather
and bone; nothings ever wasted. They have aprimitive level
of technology, and so metal goods, especially weapons, are
highly prized and must be traded, stolen, or won in battle.
‘They are a dark-haired Wareran rare, tanned and weathered
by exposure to the sun and the stinging desert winds; their
clothing is mostly leather and fur, and they delight in body
painting and tattoos. Within a tribe, families are loosely orga-
nized into clanswhich are led by a sacred Khan and his herd
‘queen. The men mostly worship Waha, their founding deity,
and the women worship Eiritha, the Herd Mother.

‘Praxians are conservative and traditional, following
Waha’s ancient laws. They value courage and honesty above
all else; the latter is demanded from members of the same
tribe, expected fiom members of other tribes, and withheld
from non-Praxians who are viewed with suspicion and scorn.
‘Horses are taboo for Praxians and they cannot be eaten or
ridden. Horse riding tribes like the Pol-Joni and the Pentan
nomads are especially hated, almost as much as Chaos.

Note that when creating Men-and a-half characters, use the Taller
modification to Characteristic SIZ, whereas members of the Impala,
Bolo Lizard and Ostrich tribes should use te Smaller modification, as
described on page 24.

SARTARITE (HEORTLING)
CULTURE

"All peoplecan be great if they follow the virtues of Onlanth: cour-
cage, wssdom, generosity justice, honour and piety So say I, Agi Har
banisson, thane of the Varmandi."

Sartar is the last bastion of free Onlanthi resistance to the
relentless march of the Lunar Empire. [t comprises of 24
proud tribes who have lived in the Dragon Pass region for
just over 300 years. The House of Sartar resisted the Lunars
fora century or so, until it fell to a major assault led by the

Geom En OurxamRVxzOD

### Page 36
ADVENTURES IN GLORANTHA& CHARACTERS: +

Red Emperor in 1602. Despite the House of Sartar having
fallen, the remaining tribes remain steadfast in defending
their freedom and way of life from Lunar impesition.

The Sartarite culture originated in the Dragon Pass
and Holy County regions of Genertela in the Storm Age:
many Orlanthi of the Sartar regions still call themselves
Heortlings after the Silver Age hero. During the First Age,
they expanded to dominate Genertela, In Umathela, in
north-western Pamaltela, a migrant population of Orlanthi
still survives. Most Orlanthi live in humble, scattered villages.
‘Towns tend to be few and modestly sized (although same
significant exceptions exist, such as the great metropolis of
‘Nochet). Very few people can read; the cult of Lhankor Mhy
holds a monopoly over professional scribes.

All members of Sartarite society begin within a dan orga-
nization, with clans forming temporary or permanent tribes.
Ina fewregiong tribes have formed confederations which are
known as kingdoms, The Sartarites practice mixed agricul-
ture and pastoral herding. Farm land is gifted by the clan to
each free farmer in small field strips, each about the size a
plough team can work in a day or so. The fields of a single
farmer are typically scattered throughout the clan lands and
marked by low walls built fiom the stony ground. Many dans
also have small fruit orchards and vineyards that are worked
by individual families, usually for many generations
at crans ‘The clan is the basic operative social unit. Smaller units,
RangedMarisman, Whether bloodlines or households, and larger units, whether

Skirmisting tribes or kingdoms, all come and go, but the clan is steadfast.

It may prosper or diminish, butt does not change its require
_ ments and definitions Clans are the ultimate keepers of the

Assassination, farm and pastoral lands which the peoples occupy. No indi-
vidual ever owns land, though they might daim many rights
to use the land by virtue of previous usage and from clan
decisions, either traditional orrecent,

‘Members of the Sartarite dans usually participate in all
social, political and religious fimctions of their particular
region. They are keen and active to be heard, and cast a
vote in the formal ritual of “Weapon Taking”, wherein adult
members must present their tools of achulthood for inspection
to qualify for being considered a member able to cast a vote.

Sartarites are skilled livestock raisers, especially sheep and
cattle: sheep typically graze in the hills, cattle in the lowiands.
Horses are highly valued as mounts. In Dragon Pass, the Holy
(Country; and parts of the Lunar Empire, Praxian beasts are
also usedas mounts and as livestock. The Ortanthi make use
of a domesticated feline called an “aly”, or “Shadowcat”,

for tasks given eleewhere to dogs especially herding and
hunting The Sartarites ame sophisticated crafters and highly
regarded as redsmiths, weavers, and potters. They learned
the art of metalworking from the dwarves (who taught the
god Gustbran).

‘Being a widespread culure, appearance and dress can
vary considerably, but most Sartarites have dark or red hair,
olive or tanned skin, and brown and blue eyes, They have a
ready wit, passionate natures and, as befits worshippers of the
tempestuous storm god Orlanth, a tendency towards reck-
lessness and hotheadedness. "Violence is always an option"
is an oft-quoted Orlanthi maxim, and for the Sartarites it is
very true; however it also belies the fact that Orlanthi are
alan sociable, considerate and have very sophisticated laws
regarding hospitality and generosity towards strangers.

Sartarites like to adorn their bodics with tattoos Each
clan and tribe has its own tattoo; these help distinguish indi-
viduals quickly when first meeting, and of course, during
battle. At initiation, new adults are marked with their clan
designs, as well as the marks of the gods and personal runes.
Status, profession, and important life events are also marked
with tattoos Odanthi tattoos can be located on many places
of the body: the face, shoulder arms, legs, the back, the
abdomen, and so on, but are usually prominent so that their
culture and affiliations can be easily seen and understood.

LANGUAGE

‘The Sartarites speak a family of closely related languages
called Theyalam. All Theyalan languages are written using
the Three Sacred Scripts of Lhankor Mby, which were cre-
ated by him in the God Time, and are the same in all Orlan-
thi lands.

Murnulvretan: alo called “Cat Scratching”, this flow-
ing and ornate script is used primarily by the Orlanthi of
Dragon Pass, Holy Gountry and East Ralios

Flasa Secrets: also called “Stone Scratching”, this
scriptisextremely difficult to learn, andis used only for mag-
ical formulae. This script uses the second vocabulary, whose
‘words change in meaning according to a complex code sys-
tem that must be learned separately.
Macic

‘The Sartarites worship the pantheon of gods known as
the Storm Tribe, and are first and foremost Theists, calling
upon their gods to channel Rune Magic. though the ances-
tors of the dan are venerated and remembered at Sacred

Animists (although there are Orlanthi shaman who can and
do commune and bargain with certain spirits on behalf’ of
the clan). Sorcery is mistrusted and shunned; mysticism is
not practiced and viewed withsome suspicion.

(Clans AND Sociat STATUS

Sartarite clans range in size fiom as fw a3.500 to as many
as 2000 people. Communities much smaller than that cannot
maintain'the clan's magic in the long term, and larger com-
munities will be too riven by internal conflicts to maintain a
truly unified identity. Clan Resources do not dictate its size;
there are small clans with great Wealth or Military might, and
Jarge clans that are poor or lacking good warriors.

‘The average Sartarite clan has about 900 people. Approxi-
mately half of the clan are adults and about | im 12 are edders
over the age of 60 years, The rest of the clan is children and
othernot adults, Approximately half the clan is male and the
other half is female. A minority of either gender serves in a
role normally associated with the opposite gender (e.g,, war-
ior women or male healers):

Normally, about | in 7 of the clan adults are leaders and
other specialists (thanes), about 3 im? are free farmers (carl),
and the rest are dependent farmers and herders (collectively
called cottars), The precise ratios vary from dian to clan.

At the very top of the clan is the clan Chiaftain (Dai).
‘The chieftain has 1 hides of land and sizable herds of lve-
stock allocated for to support him and his household.

Thanes, also called “Horse Men”, are those folk with a
leadership role in the clan: the bodyguards of the chief, the
priests, the heads of households and bloodlines, the members
of the clan council and others who have been given unusual
and important responsibilities within the clan. Among their
responsibilities include being the first ones to go to war. As
a result, fighting is almostalways their primary or secondary
occupation and thanes are well equipped, trained and ready
to fight whenever necessary. Thanes are allocated herds of
livestock and about five hides of land and herds of livestock
to support them and their household. A typical dan has
around 30 to 50 thanes.

Carls, also called “Cattle Men™, are the free folk of the
clan, with the widest range of legal rights and responsibilities.
‘They own a whole ox-team and a plough, and are allocated
one hide of land to support and their family Carls own some
military equipment and use it to defend the clan whenever
the chief orders it. A typical clan has about 100 carl families.

Cottars, also called “Sheep Men”, are the lowest class of
free folk. They have no lands allocated to them, and instead
work the lands and herd the lvestock of others.

TARSH CULTURES

The Kingdom of Tarsh, north of Sartar, is the largest
country in Dragon Pass and firmly part of the Lunar Empire,
being its richest Province; it includes the upper reaches of the

GFGHewmeInOnixreamegvszoo

### Page 39
s ADVENTURES IN GLORANTHA & CHARACTERS:

Ostir and Black Fel rivers, and the high valleys around Kero
Fin. Originally Tarsh was settled by Orlanthi settlers from
South Peloria after 1330. Once centred on the valleys to the
north and west of Kero Fin, the core of the kingdom is now:
the Osiir River valley near the Lunar city of Furthest. Tarsh
has redaimed the northern part of Sartar as its own, setting
the Tarshites in direct opposition with the Sartarite Orlan-
thi, However, not all Tarshites have submitted to the Empire;
the Exilesare a harsh, ruthless group of mercenaries, raiders
and bandits who refuse to submit to the Red Moon and its
puppet Lunar kings. They hold a precarious independence
around Wintcrtop Fort, where good defensive terrain and
the protection of the Shaker’s Temple provides them refige.

‘The King of Tarsh is tributary to the Red Emperor, pay

ing money, goods, slaves and obedience to the Empire in
the person of the Provincial Governor, whose residence is
in Mirin’s Gross, far down the Oslir River The city of Fur-
thest is the centre of Tarsh culture, built over the previous
settlement as a Lunar colony in Dragon Puss. It is the home
of the king and his family, as well as a major Seven Moth-
ers temple: Its residents, and the farmers who thickly popu-
late the river valley, are thoroughly Lunarized in attitudes,
although the lifestyle, language, and customs of the common
‘Tarshite person are Orlanthi in manner. The-clan chiefs owe
allegiance to regional leaders who used to be triballyelected,
but are now appointed by the king and so reflect the will of
the Provincial Governor and the Red Emperor. Taxes are
paid in livestock, mined goods, or other (induding slaves).

‘Tarsh consists of a mixture of inhabitants:

% Provincial Lunar settlers, who were cither born
here or moved here in recent years, perhaps at the
behest of the Provincial Governor, close family or
even the Emperor himself. Lunar Tarshites place the
Red Goddess first and foremost in their loyalties and
some also recognize the prevailing power of the Storm
‘Tribe, knowing that it is wise and prudent to continue
to acknowledge Orlanthi customs and traditions in
order to maintain the peace. There are some mili-
tants though, who believe that Orlanthi ways in Tarsh
should be curtailed. It is part of the Empire now and
the old gods must obey the Reaching Moon If thcy do
not, they will die.

% Orlanthi who have come to accept the Red Moon
and acknowledge its power andinfluence, but still hold
true to Storm Tnbe ideals and customs. The King
of Tarsh and his family are a good example of such

Our thtH @TAA Awe wR

Orlanthi Tarshites who recognize and reconcile both
the old and the new

& The Exiles who reject and rebel against the Lunar
Imperialist invaders and want to see Tarsh freely
reunited with Sartar and returned to the Storm Tribe
completely. The Lunar Empire is a hated enemy and
its agents deserve no mercy.

Tarsh is therefore a volatile crucible of cultures. The
moderate Lunar Tarshites and Onanthi Tarshites manage
to coexist quite peacefully and happily. The fringe elements
though, would see the other side either brought to heel,
expelled or exterminated and view the moderates as weak
kneed appeasers that lack the strength of true commitment
to one side or the other.

‘Tarsinte CHARACTERS

If creatinga Tarshite character, choose dither the Lumar
Provincial or Sartarite culture and then decide which
side of the spectrum his or her loyalties fall: Radical Funar,
Moderate Lunar, Moderate Orlanthi or Orlanthi Exile.
‘This political position will not affect the skills deriving from
the cultural background, although it will affect the charac-
ter's Passions and general outlook.

can wield simple and powerful magic.

‘What really differentiates them from other primitive cul-

with their beast-brothers is deep and profound, and the
Hsanchen believe that they have the same souls with their
animal brethren; some groups-view themselves as animals

A bag of old bones has been in your family for generations. It is claimed that the bones belong to a great hero of your people. As such the
bones are sacred relics and must always be treated with reverence. Occasionally, your grandmother would set the bones ina line and chant
prayers over them. You always thought she was a bit strange. Then, a few years ago a priest came to your home and demanded to see the
bag of bones. Your grandmother brought them forth and the priest gazed into the bag. He let out a terrified scream, dropped the bag, and
fled from your home. When you looked in there, the bones appeared to be quite normal. Now the bag isin your possession. What caused
the priest to flee? What do the bones mean? Who did they belong to? Why do they occasionally rattle of their own accord?

You have eyes of quite different colours. This may be the result of a childhood accident, illness, or simply a quirk of nature. It makes you

Money &
EQUIPMENT

“Above is the rune of Issaries, the God of Trade. Initiates of his cult are merchants and heralds, protected by their god's
reputation and power. Issaries' cult is popular and ubiquitous: it can be found throughout most of the civilised world.

Jorantha's eceonomy, coinage and essentiak of

daily life are covered in this chapter, including price

- ists for commonly (and not so commonly} available

goods and services, We begin with an overview of Gloran-
than coinage.

COINAGE

Lunars
‘The Lunar is the equivalent of the RuxeQuesr Silver
Piece and in Glorantha, the Lunar has a generally higher
purchasing power than the default RuNEQuEsT coinage. Far
mostitems, dividing the Rune Quesr price by five is a reason-
able rule of thumb. A single Lunar typically represents:
% 1 day’s wage for a dkilled worker
% The daily cost of living for a man of property
& The daily cost of living for a poor family (2 adults and
their children)
% A peck (6.67 kilos) of grain, enough to grind flour for
up to 20 loaves of bread

OuUrkt th FTAA AGB

Gow Wiens -

‘Gold Wheels are hardly ever seen, and even more rarely
used, as they are primarilya Yelmalion currency. One Wheel
typically represents:

& The weekly living cost of a rich man

% The monthly wage of a lowly henchman

& The cost of a smart banquet for 5 people including

high quality wines, a variety of meat and fish, serving
staff andentertainment

Ciacks

‘Lowest valued of the coins, the copper Clack has retained
the same notional value over the centuries, so there are many
very old, worn coins still in circalation. One can purchase a
loaf of bread for a single Clack, and two loaves of bread is
enough to provide the necessary calories for an adult human
to get through the day.

LIFESTYLE AND
Cost OF LIVING

‘As the Lunar has greater buying power than the standard
Silver Picce, the starting money determincd during character
creation should be adjusted to take into account the Gloran-
than economy. The Starting Money for characters is based
on their culture and is found on page 24 of the Character
Creation chapter.

EARNING A LIVING
Being in paid employment is oftenan uncertain situation,
with job security being a xeward for loyalty rather than an
expectation. Most jobs pay enough to keep the employee in
_ an acceptable standard of living, but if the employee has oth-
ers to support, it is frequently not enough. For this reason it
can be necessary for anyone who is old enough to conuibure
to the household income in some way.

towns may havesome of these things available, perhaps

@& Rare items are usually found only in a city, and prob-

ox regions ~ such as Praxian tribal gatherings,

even then, one that sits dose to the pointof ongin oris

CLOTHING

Some basic items can cost a considerable proportion of
earnings. Clothing in particular is an expensive necessity;
hence the poorest folk and slaves might have no more than a
simple shift of unbleached wool to their name, or even same-
thing sewn together from scraps. The destitute might still get
hold of animal skins, which are cheaper than woven doth.

Good clothes truly mark out an individual as sameone of
means. The quality of the doth, the we of dyes and addi-
tional embellishments such as embroidery, fringes or even
Ete metal adomments sewn into the cloth are all dues to the
status of the wearen

helmet, and perhaps a sidearm such asa short sword. Pre-
ferred armours aré pad ded and quilted cloth, typically linen
stuffed with wool, or scale armour made from leather, horn
or metal, or same form of composite combination.

LAND AND PROPERTY

Farm land is measured in very practical terms by the
Orlanthi areas are measured in terms of how long it takes
to work with a plough team of four to eight oxen. The
ploughman (usually the car or senior farmer), and the ox-
driver (usually his wife orson}, guides the plough. Many lands
also include small fruit orchards and vineyards. Although the
following measures are Orlanthi in nature, they have been
largely adopted across Genertela as standards and the Lunars
have not attempted to replace the system with anything else

An acre is the amount of land tillable by ane ox-team
in one day — about half a hectare.

®% A hide is m amount of land that one ox-team can
plough in a year and is considered sufficient to support
an Oflanthi carl and his household. It is between 80
and 120 acres(40 and 60 hectares). The Lunarsvaluea
hide at 25 Wheels for census purposes.

& Five hides is the amount of land consdered sufficient
to support an Orlanthi thane and his household. This
much and typically requires four or five tenant families
to work; the tenants are cottar clients of the thane.

Bach acre planted for wheat should ddiiver, on average,
anet 12 6usheds atharvest time after setting aside the
next year's seed corn, which equates some 50 Lunars
of earnings for the farmer -

The Oxlanthi, who are experts on working the land, agree
that the right size plot to support an average family is about
25 acres. One might need a bit more if not all the land is
good for grain, adding up to 5-12 acres of arable pasture and
orchard.

Proximity to a temple or sacred site that provides reliable
divine blessings will increase land prices, because miracles
may be available that restore ferdlity to tired soil without lea
inga field fallow.

‘The cost of dwellings is for something built to order or
already standing, In the countryside, most people build their
own simple houses at minimalcost and pass them on tofuture
generations, who then fight to keep them standing until it
reaches the point when it is easier to plunder the ruins for
building materials and start over.

An acre of good arable land requires 10 Lunars worth of
seed corn and will deliver a yield of six times the seed sown,
generating a net return worth 50 Lamars. In particularly good
soils or with generous magical support, it is possible to as
much as double that return.

New WEAPONS

‘Most weapon types found in the RuneQuesT rules have
their equivalents in Glorantha, including crossbows (which
are an invention of the Mostali, along with limited black
powder weapons). Below am several new weapons not
detailed in the main rulebook.

CLOsE COMBAT WEAPONS

‘The sickle sword and Khopesk are weapons of the Lunar
amny, but have been adopted by others. The sickle sword is
an adaptation of the agricultural tool for battlefield use; its
wicked, crescent moon blade is designed to slash and gouge,
giving it the Bleed and Sunder Special Effects. The khopesh
also has a curved blade, but the curve isnotas pronounced as
the sickle sword, and the blade is heavier, with a thick, Hunt
edge facing the wielder, anda hooked point thatis perfect for
hooking onto both close combat weapons and shields. Lanar
cavalry tend to prefer the khopesh over the sickle sword,
while the infantry like the vicious balance of the sickle sword
over the heavier khopesh.

‘The fonios is a very long cavalry lance designed for use
with both hands while the mount is steered with the knees. It
is popular among the Lunar cavalry but isalso found among
some Praxian and Pentan nomads.

GLORANTHAN SHIELDS

‘The following shields have been added to represent those
available to various Gloranthan cultures. All are held with a
centre-grip, save for Dara Happan Hoplons, and Praxian,
‘Western Cavalry and Western Infantry shields, which are:
strapped to the forearm (granting a bonus of one difficulty
* grade against the Disarm special effect).
Dara Harran HoPLon

A modes-sized strapped hoplite shield, with a small
cut-out on the edge where the wielder can support a two-
handed spear or sarissa without exposing their hand. Made
of bronze-faced wood, they are enamelled with the insignia
of the regiment to which they belong:
ORLANTH ROUND SHIELD

Mainly used by the farming and crafting classes when
mustering for war, this plain wooden shield is found almost
everywhere throughout Orlanthi lands. The majority are
decorated with personal painted devices or bronze appliqué.

OUrkt hh OTAAA DEK

56

ORLANTEA SCUTUM.

Large oval shiclds used by professional weapon thanes
and nobles. They are made from laminated wood with a
bronze rim and shield boss for extra strength. As with all
high-status Orlanthi possessions, the metal work is ornately
decorated.

PELORIAN ASPIS

A large circular and dished aspis for maximal protective
defence. Like the Dara Happan hoplons from which they
evolved, @ typical Lunar army aspis is bronze faced and
rimmed for toughness, with enamelled regimental insignia.
PELORIAN PELTAST SHIELD

‘Used by lighter troops, this wooden shield, reinforced
with a bronze rim and boss, has the distinctive crescent
moon shape synonymous with the Lunar army: They are
usually painted with regimental insignia.

PRAXIAN SHIELD

Small, round shields made from the stretched hide of
whatever tribal beast the wielder belongs to. Lacking much
in the way of metal or paint, most Praxians decorate their
shiclds with daborate collections of bones, beads and feath
ers. Due to their size and the way they are strapped to the
forearm, Praxian shidds cannot be used to passively block
damage to the legs when dismounted.

Rone.

Glorantha is not Earth, and its metals are analogs, not
duplicates, of Earthly metals. All metal comes from the
bones of gods, some dead and some still living. Bronze is
the most common metal, mined directly from the earth in

MAacIc

Glorantha’s magic is introduced in this chapter, with the chapters following it describing the specific magical approaches in

greater detail.

loranthans practise many different types of magic
which anyone can learn, provided they arc of the
‘correct species, ethnic culture or members of a cult
‘which teaches it. Thesearts are called are Folk Magic, Spirit
Magic, Rune Magic, Sorcery and Lunar Magic. The
incomprehensible art of Mpsticisems is primarily reserved for
the Draconic races.
‘As described in chapter XOX, all magic is drawn from the
Runes; the fundamental building blocks of Gloranthan reality
* Certain cultures and species possess inherent bonds to certain
Runes, called Rune Affinities, which often limit the cuks, tra-
ditions and schools which they may join - and in tum restrict
the particular spells or spirits which they can then master.

FoLk Maaic

(ROP Battle Magis, ROY Shirt Magi, ROG Falk Magic)

Folk Magic is the simplest form of magic in Glorantha,
commonly available to all cultures. It is taught from an early
age, butin terms of power offers only limited effect. Particular
spells reflect the everyday necessities of a community, profes-
sion or cult which provides them. This means that Folk Magic
taught to a barbarian goat herd will often differ to that taught
to a civilized sailor. Due to its petty nature, Folk Magic spells
are not owertly supernatural, instead tending to augment natu-
ral processes, the surrounding environment or the capabilities
of the caster.

OWrrt tm SFA A Ao BK

59

Rune Maaic

(RQ2 Rune Magi, RQ3 Divine Magic, ROG Theism)

‘Rune Magic is drawn fom the gods, demi-gods and heroes
of Glorantha, provided the worshipper performs the cor
rect rituals to invoke the deity and performs regular sacrifices
to honour or propitiate them. In effect, the god intercedes
directy on behalf of the worshipper; either locally manifest-
ingthair power through a Rune they are linked with, or incar-
nating directly within the body of the worshipper to perform
an epic feat. Duc to the ubiquity of religious cults across the
world, Rune Magic is the most frequently encountered higher
magic in Glorantha.

SORCERY

(ROB Serer, ROG Sorcery)

‘A less well regarded form of magic by many, sorcery uses
immutable laws to exploit the Runes directly, without need-
ing to call upon the gods or bargain with spirits. Such spdls,
are impersonal and formulaic, normally controlling only the
material aspects of the world. Yet sorcery is feared by those
practicing Spirit and Rune Magic, since sorcerers are capable
of briefly changing the nature af local reality or even drain-
ing its energies at the cost of destroying whatever is tapped.
Fortunately however, although very potent, sorcery spells are
usually limited in application.

Sea rxnOWw rx omevsz OO

### Page 61
R ADVENTURES IN GLORANTHA R Macic

Spirit MAcic

(RQG Animism)

A higher magical discipline, Spirit Magic is the practice
of dealing with the spirit world and those spirits that are
bound to the mortal realm in some form. Spirit magicians,
or Animists, form relationships with particular spirits which
work their supemaitural effects.on behalf of the magician or
the community which they serve. Each spirit controls one
or more specific eflect(s), based upon natural processes of
the world. Alll things, be they animate or inanimate, are pos-
sessed of a spirit — from the smallest of flowers to an entire
mountain. The spirits of sapient creaturcs still bound to a
mortal body are called souls.

LUNAR Maaic

Last, but by no means least, is the odd and disturbing
higher art of Lunar Magic. This type of magic gains its eso-
teric power from the Moon Rune, itself a strange facet of
both Glamour and Chaos. In practice, those following the
Lunar path are able to cheat the Great Compromise to call
upon a wide array of powers, albeit at dightly less strength
than other magical practitioners, depending on the phase of
‘the Red Moon. However, those who dabble in Lumar Magic
are prone to [lumination, and this often draws the hatred of
other less open-minded cultures.

MysTIcisM

(ROG Myssicim)

‘The study of mysticism in Glorantha is limited to only
those of Draconic blood or those deluded enough to become
subservient to them. This however is a blessing in disguise,
as Mysticism is perhaps the most potentof the magical arts,
quite capable of radically and irrevocably altering the entire
universe at the whim of the mystic, usually to the detriment
of everyone else, since most practitioners believe alll exis-
tence is merely an illusion that must be cast off before they
can transcend to a higher state.

CONVERTING OLDER

Source MATERIAL

Earlier editions of RuneQuesr produced a great many
different spells and spirits which no longer quite conform to
the RuxeQuest 6th Edition rules. Despite extensive work
revising material from previous editions, converting cults and
characters still requires some effort ftom the Games Master
in order to redress both mechanical changes to the rules and
conceptual changes to Glorantha itself.

To ease this process, the magic chapters either offer aref
erence to the revised spell in the RUNEQueSsT 6th Edition
Core Rules, or provide an entirdy brand new version. It
must be noted that in a few cases the changes are radical in
nature, due to the prior reasons offered.

GENERAL RULES FOR
GLORANTHAN MAacic

‘The following mechanics are offered merely as guide-
lines, and should not be treated as hard and fast rules if a
Games Master wishes to retain an earlier play style in their
game. For ease of description, the following section uses the
word ‘spells’ by default, meaning spells, spirits or techniques,
according to the type of magic utilised.

CHANGES TO CASTING SKILLS

Since access to magic in Glorantha is via the Runes, the
skills required to cast and manipulate some forms of magie
have been revised to take into account the importance of
Rume Affinities ee Chapter XX).

Taking Sorcery as an example, the skill of Incocation has been
replaced with whichever Rune Affinity is linked to that speil, which
in turn is jirther modified by the Four Principles (Combine/ Separate,
Command, Sunmnon/Dismiss and Tab). Shaping, on the other hand, is
‘replaced by the sorcerer's Law Rune affinity.

Careful study of these new rules will be required to avoid
confusion.

SPELLS AVAILABLE PER

TEMPLE OR TEACHER

Generally, most cults, traditions or schools offer between
1d3+4 Folk Magic spells and another 1d3+4 advanced
spells (Spirit Magic, Rune Magic, Sorcery, Lunar Magic or

Seow Cn OmrxeawmeFezO0

### Page 62
Mysticism) to their members. Not all cults are the same, how-
ever. Minor deities or hero cults might offer only a single addi-
tional spell or skill for those who desire to learn it, whereas the
greatest gods or schools can affer a dozen or more.

AVAILABILITY OF SPELLS

Generally only members of a cult, tradition or school are
permitted to learn a spell belonging to that organisation. In
addition, some spells are not available to members until a cer-
tain cult rankis achieved, to ensure they are not misused, or
that cult secrets are not, revealed to those uninitiated in the
traditions of that organisation. ‘There are always exceptions
to the rules, however; for instance the cult of a trading deity
might offer to exchange spell knowledge for other benefits.

PRICE OF SPELLS

‘Most Gloranthans must pay for the acquisition of new
spells, despite their cult membership, Such knowledge is
expensive, and can cost the equivalent of many months
income to purchase. Folk Magic spdls cost 50 Lunars (or
5 Lanars per point if using progressive Folk Magic), whilst
higher magic such as Rune Magic or Sorcery costs 500
‘Lumars to learn each spell, Yet this financial value is only an
abstraction, since the price might actually be paid for with a
private gift, a votive sacrifice, oreven as personal time offered
in service to the organisation. Only rarely does it take the
form of hard coinage.

LEARNING SPELLS

Learning a spell in Glorantha is rarely just a case of being
taught a simple magical formula which can be invoked ad
hoc. Instead # is a matter of ritual and adherence to the
tenets of that particular cult, tradition or school. However,
just because a spell is available wo the cul they belong to,
it does not mean a character is permitted to learn it. Such
tuition takes considerable tire, not only the practice of the
actual magic, but also the indoctrination of the student via
stringent tasks or Heroquests.

Again, this can be abstracted t a mere investment of time
and Experience Rolls for games in which learning is brushed
over. On the other hand, the time requirement can be uti-
lised to provide a period of adventure wherein the character
performs objectives as part of discovering and mastering ele-
ments of the new spell.

OUrkttm OtAx Ao HBR

61

CASTING TINE

‘The casting time for all magic in Glorartha is one Action
Point per Magic Point invested in the spell’ A (non-progres-
sive) Folk Magic spell for example, will only take a single
Action Point tocast, whereasa Rune Spell witha Magic Point
cost of 3 will take three Action Points to complete.

RUNNING OUT OF

Macic Points

When a character reduces their Magic Points to zero, they
must succeed in a Willpower test or collapse imsensate. If the
cost of the spell is more than the caster’s remaining Magic
Points, the magic automatically fails. Whatever the specifics,
until further Magic Points are recovered, no more magic can
‘be cast

RECOVERING Macic Points

Glorantha is rich with magical energies, but when that
energy recovers is dependent upon the mythic everits of the
God Time and personal Runic Affinities, Characters with
an affinity to the Chaos, Darkness, Death or Disorder Runes
replenish their full Magic Points with the sctting of the sun.
All others who lack those particular Runes replenish the
entirety of their Magic Points at dawn.

RESTRICTIONS ON CASTING

Magic requires freedom of movement and mind to beable
to cast a spell A caster suffers one additional difficulty grade
to their casting skill for each of the following:

& Mental Impairment. The caster is affected by magical
mental or emotional domination, narcotic substances
(including sufficient alcohol), a Serious Wound to the

Seow inOirxame ys OO

### Page 63
R Aventures 1N GUORANTHA k MAGIC

head, or any other poisons and diseases that affect
mental state.

% Physical Constriction, The caster is grappled, tied up
or loses the use of one or more limbs.

®% Verbal Restraint. The caster cannot intone due to loss
of tongue, wearing a gag or cannot breathe due to sub-
mersion or strangulation.

% Suffers Pair. The concentrationof the caster is shaken
by suffering a Minor Wound. Serious Wounds inflict
two difficulty grades, whilst Major Wounds make spell
casting impossible due to ineapacitation.

A spell automatically fails if the caster:

® Ambulates at greater than walking speed.

ais i or otherwise comatose.
% Cannot see or sense the intended target of the spell Gf
appropriate).

There are no penalties for casting in dose combat, as
many spells are intended for batde. Games Masters may
need to apply the above restrictions on a case by case basis
according to the species or abilities of the caster.

STACKING Macic

Magic of differing disciplines can be stacked together,
provided that they are both available as part of the same
cult, tradition or school the caster belongs to. In such a case
the normal restriction, that only the magic with the greater
Intensity take effect, is over-muled. Forexample, an initiate of
Humakt could combine a Bladesharp spell (Folk Magic) with
a Truesword (Rune Magic) spell to both increase the default
damage of his weapon and allow him to roll it twice.
+ Although stacking is permitted, it only apples to a single
spell of each discipline. Thus the Folk Magic spells of Blade-
sharp and Fireblade couldn't be combined together with the
‘Truesword spell.

In all other circumstances, the default rules concerning
stacking takes precedence (sce RuneQuest page 181).

GENERAL ADVICE

The new magical rules presented in Adventures in Glo-
rantha are intended for starting fresh campaigns using the
RuneQuest 6th Editiontules as a base. Garne Masterscon-
verting over legacy games may find themselves more com-
fortable simply converting over effects of existing spells from

OWUrki tes OtAx aa BH

62

previous versions of RuNeQust and avoid the mechanical
changes necessary to readjust to the current view of Gloran-
than practice

In other words, if’ you are unhappy with the new way of
doing things, then feel free to ignore the new rules as you
wish. Your Glorantha Will Vary!

FOLK MAaGiIc

AT AMR WOVAL

‘The simplest and mest straightforward of the magical approaches, folk magic can still be very powerfull when used creatively,
Every spell, no matter how basic, has its uses and a clever folk magician can work wonders with only a handful of a charms.

olk magic is the most basic form of magic, and avail-
able to just about every Gloranthan. Folk Magic is a
<Bset of common cantrips and minor magic effects that
are used on an everyday basis to help with daily life, regular
chores and, when the need calls for it, offensive and defen-
sive purposes (and why Folk Magic is sometimes called Battle
‘Magic by mercenary bands and martial cults).
Folk magic works here, now and on or against something
_ that can be seen and felt. Its effects are temporary and gen-
erally not extreme {although this depends very much on the
creativity of the caster and the circumstances for the spell).
Folk Magic is not imnate no Gloranthan is born with a set
of spells but the capacity to learn and work Falk Magic is as
natural as learning to speak. Therefore, the majority of Glo-
ranthans know a handful of Folk Magic spells and use them
regularly and assume that everyone else uses them too. The
very few who do not use Falk Magic, either because they have
not been taught any, or for other reasons, are considered to be
the exception and not the rule.

LEARNING FOLK MAGIC

Spells are a taught by word of mouth, and passed down
from generation to generation. They may be taught within a
family, from a guild or even by wandering magicians. Anyone
can learn and use a spell. There isno need to be able to read;
the character simply memorises a series of words, gestures
and mental symbols. However, if the character wishes to cast
the spell at range, or to cast the spell on another living target,

Our Rt Pm. OtTAAA oo BK

63

then they must create a focus through which the spell’s energy
‘will be channelled, usually involving the Rune from which the
power is taken.

‘A focus cain take many forms; Orlanthi prefer to tattoo the
focus on their own bodies for example, bat carving the focus
into objects, weapons and amour are also popular choices
amongst other cultures. If-the focus is lost-or damaged, the
character will need to create a new one (hence the reason why
tattoos and incised designs on the skin are a popular choice
for creating foci). Although each focus is unique, it is possible
to carve multple foci for different spells into the same object.
‘However, it is not possible to create multiple foci for the same
spell; part of learning the spell consists of attuning the spiri-
tual self to a specific focus.

CASTING FOLK Macic

Folk Magic follows the usual RUNEQUEST rules, except that
the casting is considered to be an Automatic Sticoess (RUNE-
‘Quest page 57), unless the spell is cast againsta resisting tar-
get or is cast al range in which case the Folk Magic skill
must be rolled as normal. This may seem like a huge advan-
tage compared to the RuneQuesr default, but Glorantha is a
‘world suffused with magié, and the ability to be use minor folk
magic is as normal to Gloranthans as breathing.

Casting a Folk Magic spell is rarely a silent or motionless
activity Every culure has its own ways of channelling natu-
ral magical energy, but chants, dances, drones, susiitrations,
ritual gesticulations, songs, rhymes and poems are frequent.

COMPREHENSION

Touch

This spell increases the target’s mental capacity, so that
the next JNT-based skill check made by the recipient is one
difficulty grade easier {provided they know that skill). INT-
based skills are those which use INT to calculate their base
value, such as Deceit, Perception or Seamanship.
CONCEAL ITEM

Touch

‘This spell renders invisible one or more items with a com-
bined ENC value no greater than 3: Thus the caster could
conceal a backpack full of tools, or that they are carrying
around a forbidden weapon. The only time such objects
become visible is if the caster openly interacts with it, for
-example if a concealed weapon is drawn anid used to attack.
In such cases, the object returns to obscurement once the
interactionceases.

Ranged

Olrkrttwers. STtTAAAG ER

64

DARKWALL

Renged

Dariewall creates an area of shadow, equal to the caster’s
POW in square metres (and a default height of one third
of their POW), which suppresses all light within it. This is
enough volume to fill a modest room, a length of corridor
or form a small cloud if cast outside. All non-magical light,
including sunlight, passing into or present within the bound-
ary is reduced to the equivalent of a dim glows so that it can
be seen, but provides no illumination to see by. Other senses,
such as sound, are unaffected by the shadow A Darkwall
can be moved or shaped into the depth or width desired, so
Jong as the total area is equal to the caster's POW in square
metres,

DELAYED IGNITE

Touch

Developed for same nefarious purpose by the Mostali,
this spell works exactly like Ignite (RuNEQuesr page 191)
except that it can only be cast on objects the user is touching
The object will then burstinto flames anywhere from | Tarn
to five minutes later, at the caster's discretion. The spell can
be cast upon an abject someone & carrying or wearing, pro
vided the user can touch the item.

DETECT

See Find (RUNEQUEST page 189).

‘There are countless Detect spells and they work in the
same way as Find X in the RuNeQuest rules. Gloranthans,
however, always use some form of focus or fetish for the
spell (a wand of willow, a lodestone, a marble and so on)
that offers a tangible indication of the subject’s location. The
focus guides the caster to the closest instance of the Detec-
tion subject within range (forexample, Detect Enemy always
has the focus point move towards anyone who knowingly”
intends to harm the caster).

Note that the Detect spells can be very specific. A Detect Magic spell
indicates the closest source of magic, which, in a world like Glorantha,
is not akvays very helpful A Detect Sorcery spell though, will indicate
the nearest sorcerer or sorcerus spell (assuming one is within range).
Likewise there are separate spells for Detecting Iron, Gold, Chaos the
Undead, and s0 on.

Although generally very reliable, the Detect spell can be

blocked by dense or thick materials such as metal, earth or
stone at least one metre thick.

Detecnion BLANK

RUNE MAGIC

The Storm Rune, representative of the Onlanthi culture. They place a premium on bravery, generosity, and honour; their first
sacred law is “No One Can Make You Do Anything”, the second: “There is Always Another Way”.

n Glorantha, the gods and their manifestations are real.
Save perhaps for True Dragons, Gods are the most potent
beings in the universe. There is a hierarchy among dei

ties, ranging from Great Gods such as Humakt down to tribal

ancestors, transcendedherocs andstil-mortal demi gods. Any
of these may be the object of a Rune Cult — though a domi-
nant god ¢an lend far more powcr to its initiates than a weak
one can. Worship of a god consists of sacrifices to strengthen
the deity, in return for guarantees that the god will deliver its

RUNE CULTS

A Rune Cub is an association of individuals who gather
together, providing worship or propitiation to a particular
deity: The cult maintains the ritualsand responsibilities far its
god, offeringup sacrifices and caring for its shrine. Each cult
possesses a priesthood that officiates at sacred rituals and acts
as the intermediaries between the cult members and the god.

‘Gults are usually constrained to particular regions or peo-
ples, their temples located at sacred sites where the deity was
active during the God ‘Time. A single god may have several
different aults dedicated toit. However, not all gods have cults;
and some are found only at a single location.

Cults may be divided into three classes, depending on how
widely worshipped the god is, and how powerful it is. There
are actually several interrelated factors, as a god draws its
power from being worshipped.

OuUrnt te STAAA wD RR

69

* The first and most powerful are cults devoted t one-of the
great gods. These deities are the owners of particular Runes,
and are known everywhere in Glorantha (sometimes by other
names). Examples of this sort of cult are the cults of Ernalda
and Orlanth. A major cult will have hundreds of thousands
of worshippers across the world, and a large hierarchy with
many temples, most of which contain shrines to associated
deities, spirits andcult heroes.

‘The second type of deity has tens of thousands of worship-
pers, of which cults like Babetster Gor or Humakt are prime
examples. Whilst they still possess enough popularity to estab-
lish and maintain emples, their modest size usually predudes
shrines to assocated gods. What shrines do exist are limited to
their own cultspirits and heroes.

‘The third class of cult iscomposed of minor deities, whose
combined worshippers rarely rise to the thousands ‘These
offer propitiation to founding ancestors, subsidiary cult heroes
and powerful spirits who have not managed to make the jump
to godhood. Minor cults never own their own temples, and
indeed often have noactual priesthood. Lanbrilis an example
of a minor alt. The personality cults of still Eving demigods
can be counted amongst these.

TEMPLES

A temple is a holy place, consecrated to and protected by
agod or gods. They typitally have their own guardian entity
and sacred objects. Temples are supported by the local oom-
munity, being an important souree of specialised magical
resources. Not all temples require a building; many Orlanthi
temples for example are natural places that provide'access to

Feat nOnreaomevsz OO

### Page 71
ADVENTURES iN GLORANTHA G RUNE MAGIC

OuWrkt tm. S TAA Ao BR

7o

the Otherworld, such as hilltops, notable trees or suunding
stones. Some are even mobile like the wheeled oxcarts of
Lokamos that travel from place to place.

Most temples are served by full-time priests assigned to
the sacred site, placing themselves at the behest of worship-
pers. Shrines are similar to temples save that they are smalics,
often lacking a dedicated priest to maintain them. But in
return, they offer acoess to lesser known magics, due to some
mythic deed performed on that specific spot,

PRiEsTs

Priests are people with the full-time occupation of lead
ing magical activities. In Glorantha, the title of Pricst is a
profession, rather than a cult rank. They are responsible for
maintaining cult holy places and regalia, performing sacri-
fices and key rituals, requesting divinations and organizing
the support of the cult.

All priests are important people in the community, sus
tained by their cult members. Some priests awe their posi-
tion to their devotion or magical affinities, others to their
knowledge of cult rituals and myths, still others to their
bloodline or reputation. They are fully supported by their
local community, being given land, herds and some portion
of all sacrifices made to the gods. Because of this, priests are
ina position to devote their lives fully to their god if they so
wish.

RuNE Cutt STRUCTURE

Gloranthan alts posses a universal hierarchy which

divides their worshippers into three broad groups, as
described in the following sections: Lay Members, Initiates
and Devotees. Despite this apparent ubiquity, cults have
their own rank titles, membership requirements and duties
which can vary wildly.

ComMMUNITY
Area (Metres), Cast 2, Driration (Hows), Rank Initiats, Runes 1M,

This spell guarantees easy communication of ideas, facili-
tating the sharing of new or troubled thoughts. It afiecis every
individual within range who belongs to one of the same com-
mumities'as the caster All IN'Trelated skill rolls (providing
the user knows that skill) are automatically successful when
utilised to advance the common interests of that community.
A “community” in assumed to be a group no larger than sev-
eral hundred members, such as a family clan, village, town
district, cult, school, guild or even mercenary company.

CONCEAL/CONCEALMENT

Cost 3, Duration (Minutes), Ranged (Metres), Rank Devotee, Runes

Conceal renders the recipient both invisible and inaudible
for the duration of the spell, provided they perform no offen-
sive or destructive action. If so, the concealment temporarily
fades, revealing them to observers until they cease whatever
action revealed them, at which point they fade back into invis-
ibility at the end of the round. For the purposes of combat,
the recipient must first disengage from their opponent before
they can disappear again.

CONSUME

Cost 1, Duration (Terns), Ranged (Metres), Rank Initiats, Resist
(Endurance), Runes ¥, ‘w

If the targetiiils to resist, Consume inflicts 143 damage to
a random Hit Location, ignoring all armour On each subse-
quent turn of the caster, the target takes another 1d3 dam-
age to the same place, continuing until the location reaches
a Major Wound. At this point it is utterly destroyed, turned
into grey slime, possibly killing the target if it was a vital loca-
tion. If the spell ends prematurely before turning to slime,
any damage done can be healed normally.

Q ADVENTURES IN GLORANTHA & Spirit MAGIC

Spirit SOCIETY STRUCTURE

As with Rune Cults, every Gloranthan Spirit Society fol
lows a standard hierarchy dividing their members into three
broad groups: Fallowers, Worshippers and Shamans. Of
course, individual societies have their own rank titles, mem-
bership requirements and duties.

Sein Society RANKS

Lay MEMBERS

Cuhtures which practice Spirit Magic permit their people
to pay respect to all the major spirits within their Spirit Tra-
dition: There are no restrictions on joining a society as a lay
member, provided the character is in good standing within
the community, and none of their Rune Affinities are in
direct oppesition to those of the spirit or spirits, Thus a char-
acter can be a lay member in many societies, as such propi
tiation helps to foster good relations with the Otherworld,
‘ensuring that the entities inhabiting it continue to help, or at
least ignore, their supplicants,

Spirit Societies offer litte in the,way of mundane ben-
efits tm lay members, save for training and protection, since
membership is an expected part of everyday life. Indeed,
not participating in regular worship and propitiation tends
‘to result in being outlawed for courting disfavour from the
spints. Magical benefits are restricted to learmng the Folk
‘Magic of the Spirit Society they are a lay member of, ar ask-
ing shamans to intercede on their behalf.

Aspart of their duties, a ay memberis expected to attend
Holy Day celebrations and make a sacrifice of a few Magic
Points to restore the strength of the bound spirits belong-
ing to the worshippers and shamans of the Spirit Society. In
addition, they are expected to provide regular contributions
of food and propitiation objects to help support the higher
ranks.

OuUrnt tne @FAA ABE

-rngh

136

INITIATE

‘Becoming an initiate of a Spirit Society is a setious com-
mitment, for it requires pledging oneself to the support of
a single, albeit great, spirit. The initiate must swear to fol-
lowthe will of the spirit as expressed by the shamans of the
society, rigorously participate in Holy Day rituals, and are
expected to sacrifice a large proportion of their time to that
spint alone. Characters aan start out as an initiaté if they
possess at least five of the socicty’s
important skills at 50% or better, one
of which mostbe the Sprit Rune affin-
iy

With the Spirit Rune affinity comes
the ability to hear, see, and communi-
cate with spirits, although in and of
itself it grants no special persuasive
powers in dealing with them. The Spirit Rune allows spirit
magidans to interact with the spirits of objects, plants and
animals a3 per the Trance skill (RuneQuesr page 199). It
also replaces Binding sill when battling spirits, since this skill
isno longer used (see Gloranthan Spirit Combat page 139).

In addition, an initiate learns secrets of how to placate
and utilise spirits belonging to their Spirit Society via charms.
Initiates may possess a masinum number of bound spirits
upto half their CHA characteristic. Any more than this and
the existing spirits will leave or rebel as per their nature (see
Limits to Bound Spirits, RuneQuesr page 207).

‘The chance of persuading the spirit of a charm to per-
form a task no longer depends on the defunct Binding skill,
but now uses the Rune Affinity the magician shares with the
spirit, So an initiate of Kolat who wished to command an
elemental spirit of storm would need to succeed in a roll
against their Air Rune affinity (6). Likewise, the maximum
POW of a spirit which can be controlled is three times the
critical range of the appropriate Rune Affinity If the Air
Rume of the previously thentioned Kolati was 77%, then the
largestair elemental the initiate could command has amaxi-
mum of 24 POW.

A spirit magician who lacks the correct runic affinity will
be unable to control spirits of that Rune, yet still be able w
see and communicate with them, Whilst an Eiritha initiate
could command a herd beast spirit (¥), an accompanying
initiate of Waha would have no power over it, lacking the
Beast Rune but couldstill observeits presence and speak to
it due to the innate Spirit Rune (8) that all initiates possess.

A potent ability, the spirit gains dominion over aspects of
its Rune within a range of ten times its POW in metres. Nor
mally the limits of its influence are specified in the spirit’s
description. For example, a Plant spirit could control the
growth, flowering and fruiting of vegetation within its area
of effect, whilsta Truth spirit might prevent falschoods being
uttered, If the demesne of the spirit is challenged by a char-
acter, they may attempt to overcome it power by winning an
opposed roll of relevant Runic Affinity skills. For example,
to lie within the demesne of the Truth spirit would require
opposing the spirit’s Truth Rune with the character's Disor-
der Rune.

May move between the mundane and Otherworld at
will. Whilst in the Otherword the spirit is immune from all
attacks (magical or physical) from corporal opponents.

providing it succeeds in an attack and gains one ormore lew

rail against their Endurance skill todetermine theseverity of

Hunory Grosts (+)

‘These are Praxian spirits of the dead tied to the world of
the living because of unfinished business. ‘They lurk about
old places, trying to devour the souls of the living to appease
-their never-ending anguish. Most are lone Haunts, Wraiths,
or Death Spirits. Shamans can satiate the hunger of these
ghosts, briefly diverting their attention from the tribe by
means of a human sactifice. In most cases, the shaman uses
only volunteers or captured prisoners, but some shamans are
cormupted by the terror the hungry ghosts instil and will offer
up innocents to turn the spirits against their enemies.

LUNE AND SELENE (@)

Elemental spirits of the Redand Blue Moons respectively,
Ihnesand selenes may only be drawn from fragments brought
back from the surfaces of those inaccessible places. Sum-
moning a moon elemental requires a solid chunk of rock of
at least 6 ENC per cubic metre. Lunesand selenesshare the
same base Characteristics as other elementals (RuNEQuest

% Lunes: Away from the Red Moon, lunes are insubstan-
tial pools of pulsating red light, unable to cause physi
cal damage. Instead, they inflict madness upon those
they touch as per the Rune Magic spell (RUNEQuEST
page 272), if the victim fails to resist the elemental’s
attack roll with their Willpower.

% Scenes: Elementals of the Blue Moon, a selene is
invisible and undetectable to natural senses, making
jit especially dangerous to those without some form
of magical perception. Like lunes, a sclene cannot
inflict physical harm, instead applying its Damage roll
against the Magic Points of those it strikes.

Succusus (x)

‘A succubus is an insubstantial spirit capable of creating
a temporary body to satisfy camal desire and create trou-
ble. They appear to solitary people, such as watchmen or
night wanderers, and try w seduce the victim. They assume
the form of cither sex as appropriate. If the target fails to
resist the succubus in an opposed test of their Willpower ver
sus the spirit's Seduction skill, he will suffer the loss of 1d3
Fatigue Levels, which may only be recovered as per Blood
Loss (RuneQuesr page 108). The succubus will return each
night thereafter, until the victim is dead or manages to rebuff
her seduction attempts the latter suffering an inctementing
Difficulty Grace every evening after the first. Succubae are
Intensity 2 spirits with an INT and POW of 1d6+12, and the
spirit abilities of Knowledge (Seduction) and Manifestation.

Brotrer Dos (¥)

Predominately contacted in the Elder Wilds, Brother

canbe siimmoned at any campfire in Balazar with an offer-

return, no dog will ever harm the shaman, who, in addition
will thereafter be able to understand and speak to canines
freely.

EVENING STAR (Oa)

The lover of the sun god Yelm, Evening Star tried to fol
low him down into the Underworld but was refused at the
Gates of Dusk. Thus she waited at the edge of the world,
‘fighting off the monsters that swarmed over its rim, and even
‘tually guided the Lightbringers into Hell. In reward, she now
resides in a palace built for her in the sky where she stood
vigil. Due to hernature, Evening Star can only be summoned
once per season, at dusk urider a dear sky, coinciding with the
defeat of a creature of darkness during the ritual. In return,
she will step down from her house and shine her illumination
directly upon thc shaman and his wibe, preserving daylight
in the area until night ends at dawn. Forming a relationship
with Evening Star permits the shaman to summon her once
per week, by adopting the taboo of Never Make Deals with a
Being of Darkness.

became slave to. whoever summoned him. Now the Father
of Independents serves a8 a wretched guide across the Dead
Place in Prax, deceiving his wards with entertaining lies if
not kept tightly checked. ‘The spirit is so pathetic he answers
any summons without need of additional sacrifice, but can
somehow cross the Dead Place, where all other magic fails to
fianction. No shaman. dares form a rdationship with him, in

Mistress Cato (Gill)

A female spirit who appears garbed in wisps of shadowy
mist, her benign influence calms the dust laden airs of the dry
chaparral. She may only be summoned on days of no wind,
which normally occur only during Fire Season, In return
for gifts of flowers and song, she promises to come forth one
time when called and ward the shaman and his tribe from
any storm - even the deadly scouring simooms of Gagarth,
though not from the taste of his bitter, coppery sands. Enter
ing a relationship with Mistress Calm requires swearing the
taboo of Never Raise Your Vaicein Anger, and maintains the
protection all year round
Monkey Kine (¥4)

Almost unknown today, this obscure spizit is kept alive by
the worship of the Baboons of the Wastes. They claim the
‘Monkey King once ruleda large empire centredon the Mon-
key Ruins, destroyed in the Darkness. He is jealous of the
supremacy of humans over hiskin, and gladly emerges from
exile to strangle interlopers with his immense strength. Mon-
key King may only be summoned within Monkey Ruins. For
a baboon shaman the only cost is the taboo Never Disobey
the Monkey King, but a human shaman is forced to accept
the taboo Never Walk Upright. In retum, for each fist fall
of hair the shaman plucks from scalp or skin, Monkey King
sends a baboon spirit {equivalent to an Intensity 2 Wraith)
to aid him against his foes. These remain until the following
dawn, but never stray beyond sight of Monkey Ruins. ‘The
hair only regrows a yeararid a day later. A shaman who forms
a relationship with Monkey King may once in their life sum-
mon his physical manifestation a gigantic ape headed man
wielding a staff or mace, far beyond mortal ability to defeat
(Similar to one of The Founders, page XX).

Morninc STar (OR)

‘The younger sister of Evening Star, Morning Star brought
back the triumphant news of Yelm’s release from the Under
world. As such, she ushered in the Dawning and thereby is a
spirit of renewal and hope. Morning Star may only be sum-
moned on the last night of Sacred Time, just prior to sun-
rise, She asks nothing of the shaman, merely granting her
summoner the right to call upon her once during the follow-
ing year; as her light shines over the eastern horizon. At that
time, if facing foes of Darkness or Chacs, Morning Star will
reinvigorate the shaman and his tribe, restoring their Magic
Points back to full, returning their Fatigue levels to Fresh and
granting them courage enough to stand their ground. She

NicHt Woman (@L)

‘Night Woman brought the Darkness to Prax when she fled
up from the Underworld. The peoples of the surface fought
against her, but armed with death and winter, she was victo-
rious guarding those who submitted to her rule from the
‘Chaos that swept the lands. Since the return of the sun, her
influence has weakened, but she still covers the world half
of the time, under the folds of her velvet cloak. She can be
summoned anywhere, provided it is nighttime, with no need
for a sacrifice. There is no benefit for this, save she fredy gives
Shades to those who will accept the taboo of Never Create
a Light. Those who would form a relationship with her are
granted the ability to summon her during the day, producing
a freezing patch of impenetrable pitch darkness across the
area whilst she remains but the cost of this bond is high, as
the shaman must put out his own eyes.

Poe Star (Ol)

A famous herp, first to win back his house upon the Sky

the Star Captains. He sits at the unmoving apex of the sky,
‘watching over those who eam his ffiendship. He can be sum
moned on Fireday of Stasis Week of any season, in return for

bumed so that their spirits rise up to him. In exchange for so

Star will grant his friendship, allowing the shaman t sum-
mon and draw upon his power once per season, withoutneed
of further sacrifice.

‘The creature is able to stretch and twist parts of its phy
sique to unusual proportions. Thus a nose could elongate to
several times its length or the bones tumed floppy in order to

benefits save for adopting a revoltingly bizarre appearance.

help itslip free of manacles, stretch up to grab somethingout

The creature drains a level of Fatigue from victims, as

Fiora
‘Similar to the Undead trait, plants and other forms of ani-
mate vegetation are immune to the side effects of Fatigue and
severe injuries. Whilst a Serious Wound prevents the limb or
Jocation from functioning, the plant does not suffer any other
* debility Likewise a Major Wound does not incapacitate, nei-
ther does it immediately threaten ‘life’, although it might die
hours or days Jater. To defeat such vegetation requires thor-
ough dismemberment, or at least enough to render its offen-
sive capabilities inert.
IMMOLATE
Permits the creature to cither burst into flames itself, or
cause a victim damaged by one of its attacks to catch fire.
‘The precise details of how these flames operate art described
in the creature’s description, but the flames themselves are
rated as a specific Fire Intensity (see RuneQuesr page 121).
Anyone set alight will continue to burn until the flames are
extinguished or smothered. This takes.an Action Point to per-
form on the extinguisher’s Turn and automatically succeeds
if appropriate materials are athand for example a nearby
cloak or blanket, loose sand, sufficient water and so on. Try-
ing to smother the flames by rolling or beating them out by
hand, requires & successful First Aid (or suitably applicable
skill) roll to perform.

‘WEAKNESS

The creature possesses a particular weakness to a sub-
stance, Rune, or environment as indicated in the creature’s
descriptign. This weakness does not necessarily need to be
related to suffering damage; for instance a vampire has a
‘weakness to sunlight (amongst others) which strips many of
its supernatural powers.
