ARANDINNI
+ The Arandinni are a type of Andin demon, humanaid
of form but larger than a man, with hors and scaled skin
of iridescent colours. Residing in the Eastern Isles, their
demonic nature makes them magically potent, able to prac-
tice monstrous sorceries, despite being not as quick-witted
as humans. Indeed their bulk tends towards the corpulent,
making them rather lumbering

Like other Andin they are bound to their particular archi-
pelago of isles, unable to move beyond the narrow stretches
‘of sea which borders their dominion. They delight in play-
ing malicious tricks on the people of the Hanfarador Islands
with wham theywar Due to their proclivities they are lonely
which they lord over in empty mockery of men.

BASILISK

Noxious magical creations, formed by diabolical Hero-
quests known to cults bound to the Death or Chaos Runes.
Hatched, from eggs of dubious origin, basilisks have the
appearance of small spiny ridged ixards with the black feath-
ered heads of cockerels. Rumours of a basilisk are enough
to send most people fleeing in fear, aware that there is lit-
tle defence against its fatal stare. As such the monsters are
normally utilised as temple guardians, killing unwelcome
trespassers.

‘Their gaze is so deadly, merely staring at a victim {assum-

CHARNJIBBER

Bizarre, chaos creatures with no natural shape, charnjib-
bers are a horror found in Pamaltela. These hideous crea-
tares take on the shape of the last creature eaten, emerging
from hiding at the start of Fire Season in the form of cha-
otically warped rats or lizards, then incrementally increasing
in size as they hunt down larger quarry. After many weeks,
some have taken the form of sabretooth cap or cven dino-
saurs, but no matter what shape they subsume, they are cas-
ily identified since the new body always sports up to half
a dozen tentacles. Thankfully these monsters collapse and
rapidly decompose with the arrival of Earth Season, re-
imprisoned under the soil by the will of Pamal.

When creating one of these horrible monsters, roll 1d6.
to see how many tentacles it possesses, then 1490 for each
tentacle to see where it emerges from the original body. The
tentacle literally replaces that bit of the Hit Location,“and in
some cases entire limbs or even the head are substituted by
tentacles, although this docs not sccm to affect its ability to
catch and consume prey! A charnjibber can utilise any of its
tentacles to attack, the capabilities of the limb based upon *
the host body (relevant tables in RuneQuesr page 324).

Even without this multitude of limbs, charnjibbers
are very difficult to defeat in direct combat. Whilst Major
‘Wounds still incapacitate them, they do not die, even if the
body is completely dismembered. Instead the ‘corpse’ lies
inert until several days pass, then it devolves into an eartier
incarnation; taking the form of some smaller, previously con-
sumed prey. Dismembering a charnjibber is in some ways
more dangerous, because the individual parts each spawn a

Curr TOAD

Generally found in rocky regions, especially those provided
by mountains or ancient ruins, cliff toads use their greyish,
pebbly hides to blend into the surrounding stone. Their cam-
oullage is so good that places inhabited by these toads often
gain a reputation for being haunted, with the nearly invi-
ible toads hanging onto sheer surfaces with sucker-tippedtoes
and gulping down prey that passes too close to their prehen-
sile tongues. Whilst juvenile cliff toads are little threat save
to household pets or small children, the very largest mature
beasts are able to swallow a pony whole.

Clif toads normally attack from ambush, preventing
unaware vicims from diving aside or parrying their sticky
tongue a successfi attack resulting in the prey becoming

or faceit rested upon, out of reach of its attackers.

‘The tongue of a cliff toad can extend a number of metres

Demi-Birp

Used as mounts by the Dragonewts, demi-birds are a
throwback between a flightless bird and reptilian theropod.
‘They possess large, nasty beaks, long clawed legs and vesti-
gial wings that look like deformed arms. Despite their prime-
val appearance, their scales and plumage are quite vibrant,
the Dragonewts breeding them for colourful display, in addi-
tion to a fast loping speed and an ability to leap upon foes
in combat.

Demi-birds are mised by hand, establishing a permanent
empathic link with their rider This enables the Dragonewt
to control its mount in combat without need of reins or leg
movements, their riders gaining the Trained Beast combat
style trait for free. The link extends up to ten times the rid-
ex's POW in metres, permitting them to call their demi-bird
from afar

DREAM DRAGON

Dream dragons are the literal manifestations
of the subconscious thoughts of sleeping
‘Tme Dragons (divine entities of such size
and power they are mistaken for entire
mountain ranges). Although lesser
beasts, these embodied cogitations
take the form of formidable reptilian
creatures, driven by some esoteric phi-
losophy or base desire. As manifestations
of thought, not flesh, they slowly wax into
existence fully gown, remain for a few cen-
turies before fading from reality, perhaps to
return again.

‘The form of a dream dragon is serpen-
tine, typically between 15 and 20 metres
Jong (although smaller specimens have been
known), with four legs and wings providing flight.
In self defence most are capable of spitting one type
of weird or lethal substance depending on the whim
and Rumic relationship of the Tue Dragon. This can be
anything from burning flames to a mist of magic-stipping
venom, and affects an area as per the Breathe Flame ability
(see Rune Quest page $12}. Likewise their scales can vary in
colour and thickness, unrelated to their tize or age.

‘During their manifestation they pursue a single-minded
purpose. Usually this brings them into conflict with local
inhabitants, who rightfolly fear die dragon's destructive
capabilities. However, most dream dragons are cerebral
creatures, able to converse or lay sophisticated plans if they
so desire. Being mere figments of a sleeping Tme Dragon's
+ thoughts, dream dragons are immune to mental or psycho-
logical control, making them quite terrifying to defeat in
physical combat.

DWeERULAN

‘Dwerulan area minor subspecies of Piscoi which thrive in
the murky, stagnant Worm Sea. Their appearance is akin to
oversized humancid babies with the lower body and flattened
tail of an eel, but unlike their aquatic brethren, dwerulan
cannot breathe water and must gulp air every few minutes A
hermaphroditic species, they survive by spawning vast num-
bers of eggs, of which only a few are correctly fertilised to
continue their numbers.

‘Smaller and weaker than a man, they compensate with
cunning; utilising natural creatures such as electric eds or
poisonous jellyfish as weapons, and setting traps to soften
their victims. Their daggers and spears are fashioned from
natural armaments, for example the tail barbs of stirtgrays, or
corroded armaments looted from wrecks, In addition, their
pallid flesh extrudes a slimy coating, making them almost
impossible to grapple.

Lesser’ dwerulan are known as surutran runtish, sterile
offspring produced from self-fertilisation which barely reach
@ Quarter of the size of their parent and lack true sapience.

EARTH-SHAKERS

Gloranthan dinosaurs can be labelled as either Normal
or Original. Normal dinosaurs are ubiquitous in appearance
and tmits, being the natural descendants of other dinosaurs.
Immense herds of them roam across Pamaltela and Sion,
but can alsobe found in less dense numbers in specific areas
such as Dragon Pass, Peloria, Ralios and the Elder Wilds.

Original dinosaurs, on the other hand, arc Dragonewt
warriors which have somehow become diverted from the
draconic way, becoming entrapped in material flesh. They
often have a malicious intelligence and magical powers, and
are always carnivorous, evenif their normal descendants are
not. In such cases, convert the INS of the dinosaur to INT,
allowing it w cast spells as per a warrior stage Dragonewt.
ALLOSAURUS

Bipedal carnivorous dinosaurs formed from Dragone-
wts corrupted by greed, allosaurs average between 8 and 9
metres in length, with a long body and heay tail offering
balance. Their forearms ar short compared with their mas-
sive hind imbs, but not so short as in tyranriosaurs, The head
is large, narrow, and equipped with rows of extremely sharp
teeth.

Allosaurs atempt to disable their prey by using their foot
claws first, gripping the victim, befor rending with the teeth.
The tail lash is reserved for threats the dinosaur is aware of
that are trying to attack fiom the flank or the rear. The tail’s
size‘is enough to be able to sweep several foes simultaneously.

Macisaurus

Different from other types of Dragonewts who have fallen
from the dragon path, magisaurs are the result of damaged
dragon eggs which hatched but never evolved to the war-
rior stage. Herbivorous and freely sapient, they look just like
crested Dragonewts at hatching, but develop differently after
several years,

As they age they slowly grow larger, legs turning digiti-
grade whilst their forepaws become webbed and chunsy,
making tool use difficult. Despite this they are capable of
mastering other types of magic, since that of the dragon path
is forever lost to them. The characteristics below are for a

fully mature magisaur, the base SIZ for the initial hatchling
starting at 2d6+6.

a mob. A pteranodon usually feeds by skimming low over

favoured special effect. Creatures with a SIZ greater than its

PLESIOSAURUS

‘Swimming predators which live in the lakes and oceans,
plescsaurs are primarily located in the Swermela Sea.
‘Descended fiom Dragonewts which succumbed to aloofness,
they possess a flat broad body and four flippers that propel
them quickly through the water. Some sub-species have long,
snake-like necks, allowing them to reach up to 15m in length.
Others have shorter necks, but longer tails and heads to com-
pensate. They rarely leave the water, save to mate or bask in
the sun.

‘They hunt by pursuing shallow water or surface dwellers
at speed, but are not amiss to snatching an unwary sailor,
from the deck of a ship. The smaller heads of Jong necked
plesiosaurs reduce their damage when biting, so they tend to
use Grip to drown air breathers. Shorter necked plesiosaurs
have bigger jaws, allowing them to rip chunks of flesh free,
offen inflicting the Bleed special effect. Evade is only used
to avoid blows when it extends its head and neck above the
water, otherwise it uses its Swim skill to avoid being struck,

TRICERATOPS

Herbivorous dinosaurs created from Dragonewts tainted
by feclings of sexuality, triceratops are characterised by the
bony frill that guards their neck and the two forehead and
one nose horns with which they protect themselves. Beside
this distinctive head is the large, stocky body and short, thick
tail. Averaging around 8 metres in length, triceratops feed on
ground level vegetation and low hanging foliage with their
beaks, A triceratops may seem to be lumbering, but their
sheer weight, powerfil legs and intimidating homs mean
they are far from defenceless; a charge or herd stampede
being excellentprotection fram wouldbe predators.

GARGOYLE

‘Renowned for haunting the Rockwood Mountains and
certain ruins in Fonsit, gargoylescan be foundalmostevery-
where. Indeed, large numbers roam Slon, last remnants of
the legions created by Mostal before time began. Gargoyles
can be of almost any appearance or size, but share one
common feature: that of being made of solid stone. Their
near indestructibility and agelessness makes them perfect as
guardians for tombs, temples and forbidden places; remain-
ing stationary for such long periods of time that they are
often taken as statues.

‘The majority of gargoyles encountered are grotesquely
humanoid, combining the bestial elements of the predomi-
nant species in the region, often with additional wings and
horns. Others are quadrupeds, or perhaps lack wings alto-
gether. Although they commonly reach up to two and a half
metresin height, these ugly creatures are disproportionately
heavy. Legends of their ability to fly are overstated, more
often than not due to their practise of simply dropping from
high ledges to land atop victims However they are excellent
climbers, able to adhere tp any stone or rock surface.

Once engaged in close combat, gargoyles make no effort
to defend, instead relying on their stone hides for protec-
tion. Any weapon not designed to mine stone will suffer its
rolled damage to itself when striking the gargoyle, as per the
“Using Weapons against Inanimate Objects’ rules (Rune-
‘Quesr page 123). The following example given here is for
asmall gargoyle, waist to chest high to a man. For an aver
age (man) szed gargoyle imerease SIZ to 2d8+18 and +1
Armour Points, whilst the largest specmens have a SIZ of
2d6+30 and +2 AP; also remembering to boost Hit Points,
‘Weapon Sizes and Damages appropriately.

Ghouls, being driven by primal instincts, tend to hang
around necropolises or old battlefields for their food; although
if starving enough they will hunt for fresh meat, then let it
putrefy before consumption. Fortunately a ghoul’s howl often
gives warning of their presence, striking terror into those
that hear its inhuman wails of deranged hunger However,
the main threat posed by ghouls is their venomous bite that
inflicts paralysis.

Almost any living (or newly dead) creature relaied to the
‘Man Rune can become a ghoul, generally becoming stronger
and tougher as part of the transformation into an undead
being. Use the original Characteristics and skills of the victim,
but convert INT to INS and remove their CHA entirely. The
precise amounts the victim's STR and Armour Points rises
depends on the magic, spirit or poison used. Some ghouls
might also wear the rotted remains of armour they were bur-
ied in (-Id2 AP for decay). In addition give the new ghoul
the following Abilities: Death Sense, Terrifying (howl) and
‘Undead (Major Wound to head, chest or abdomen required
to kill).

GLARG

Reputed to be the offspring of the conjoined monster
Skanth and Skath, glargs are primarily found in Dorastor.
After birth the highly magical creatures mature in several
weeks, hut lacking sapience they are rarely capable of casting
spells, even if somebody was foolish enough to try to teach
them.

‘Standing up to four and a half metres tall, the large mon-
sters are covered with a thick shaggy pelt. Glargs umber
about on three stumpy legs spaced equidistantly about its
barrel-shaped body. They lack arms entirely, instead sporting
four grotesquely tusked heads atop long stalk-like necks. 1 in
20 hasa Chaos Feature (RUNBQUEST pages 441-442).

On asuccessfil bite, each head hangs onto the struck loca-
tion, and on the following round begins draining the STR
of the victim by Id6 points per cycle. Such STR loss is per-
manent unless cured by the Heal Characteristic spell. Those
rendered immobile fiom lost STR are dragged back to their
lair and eaten when the glargis next hungry.

GOBBLER

Semi-living constructs created by the Mostali, gobblers
are ‘programmed’ to consume specific substances precious
to their makers, to ensure the secrets of their manufacture
remain out of reachof other races. Multiple limbs surround
a huge toothed maw, into which they can shovel almost limit-
less amounts, where it is stored for processing or later regur-
gitation. Sensory organs are located in a pair of sensitive
antennae which emerge from the constructs posterior.

‘Their appetite is enhanced by eating the particular sub-
stance they seck after; the more they ingest, the hungrier and
more frenzied the gobblergets. Once ithas eaten everything,
it goes on a violent rampage sometimes devastating entire
cities in its search. The best known are Disruption Powder
Gobblers, but others have been created by the dwarfs to
ingest things like silver, adamant, or even spell matrices.

‘A gobbler’s disproportionally long legs enable them to
cover distances quickly, whilst the hand claws allow them
to burrew through earth or scale walls. Gobbler teeth are
blunt, intended to grind rather thansheer, but are capable of
crushing metal if they can gain a suitable bite angle. Once
frenzied however, they tendo be mindless combatants, seele
ing to destroy anything standing in their path, favouring
Damage Weapon or Sunder when crunching foes.

GRAYSKIN

Pitiable remnants of humans who followed the Mad Sul-
tanate into Dorastor, grayskins have devolved into an insane
and chaotically. tainted state. Harmless beasts save in mum-
bers, most encountered grayskins are those enslaved by broo
or other intelligent Chaos Races for use as food. The statistics
for grayskins are the same as a nonmal human, save that they
posses 2d6-+6 INS instead of INT, lack any CHA and each
‘possesses a Chaos Feature (RunsQuest pages 441-442).

GRIFFIN

Feature.

HEADHANGER

A headhanger is a loathsome chaotic monstrosity feared
by all right-thinking peoples. It comprises of a flaccid
wormish, insectile ar reptilian body from which sprout four
scythe-clawed limbs and countless thin stalks, some bearing
decapitated, but still living, heads These moan and shriek
insanely due to their ghastly transformation, suffering horror
at being barred from their rightful afterlife; all thoughts and
memories raped by the pallid creature, who uses the infar-
mation to garner further heads forits collection.

Instead of consuming the flesh of these stolen heads,
headhangers sup upon the entrapped soul within — slowly
draining it of Magic Points at a rate of 1 per week until the
soul is reduced to zero; at which point itis utterly destroyed
as if eaten by a Bane Spint (RuNBQuesT page 401). The
flesh left behind then procteds to slowly putrefy, eventually
rotting free of the supporting stalk. Due to this horrific diet,
a headhanger tends to hunt sapient victims, who provide it
both more nourishment, and increas¢s its own intellect.

In combat each of the headhanger’s collected heads may
make an attack, whether physical or magical. Every head uses
its own Unarmed and magical skills as appropriate, includ-
ing anyspellsit knows. Yet any Magic Paints a head expends
during casting do not recuperate. When a blow lands on one

of the creature's heads, roll randomly to

see which one was struck. A head
reduced to a Major Wound

mess, its knowledge and
skills lost but potentially
freeing what's left of
the soul. The head-

hanger itself suffers
no ill effect for the

only suffering

wounds to
its body or
limbs.

Second of the great herd beasts of Prax, herd-men are

the Morocanth, becoming the eaten rather than the caters.
‘As part of the bargain, they lost their intellect and ties to the
‘Man Rune which the tapir-like Morocanth took from them,
so are néw bred, raised and butchered as common animals,
which they have become. They primarily eat what roots and
gmibs they can scratch from the poor soil, but as omnivores
can consume almost anything

‘Herd-men have the same appearance as truce men, but
are usually identified by their lack of clothes, dirt encrusted

skin and a torpid, vacant expression on their faces. Although *

mere beasts, the Morocanth cannotride herd-men as mounts,
being too small and weak to support their master’s weight.
Tn exchange they are domestically trained to pull carts and

‘The statistics for herd-men are the same as a normal

HuAN To

A chaostainted race of horrors who reside in the foot
hills of Kralorela, the Huan To seek to overthrow the empire
that hunts them to extermination. Taller than men, their
near skeletal, animalistic heads are disproportionately huge,
as large as or larger than their torsos, with burning red eyes
and oversized fangs. Each individual's vaguely reptilian skin
is stretched across their fleshless, sinewy limbs; which end in
birdlike talons. Thus they present a farsome appearance
— one unsubstantiated as combatants, since Huan To attack
only fiom stealth or use henchmen, rarely every engaging in
frontal assault themselves.

Despite this unwilling desire to enter close combat, their
bodies possess an unnatural vitality and are resistant to physi
calinjury. Other than a subde, yet potentintellect, the great
est threat of a Huan To is a deadly magical poixon injected
via their bite. Those that fail to resist this venom are con
verted into ghouls subservient to the Huan To that bit them.
Other than this, most are proficient sorcerers specialising in
Dominate, Enslave or Tap spells.

Hypra, LESSER

Hydras are huge Chaos serpents cursed with multiple
heads and necks. Between their size and acidic venom they
are deadly foes, more than sufficient to take on a small
warband. Hydras are predominantly found in the jungles
and swamps of Pamaltela, but a few can be found in E
Slon and Dorastar too. All lesser hydra are sterile,
hatched from the eggs dropped by greater hydra. For
tunately, few of those titanic monsters exist, as they are
near impervious to mortal cambat.

A hydra can possess anywhere from 2-12 heads, each one
bearing its own Hit Points, Any detrimental effects of a Seri-
ous or Major Wound only affect the head so injured. As per
the Multi-Headed trait, every head beyond the
first adds ane additional Combat Action to the
hydra’s existing pool. Against mental or emo-
tional magic, each head is treated as a sepa-
rate target, and gains its own Will-
power resistance roll. They writhe
back and forth constantly using this
dance to’confisse prey. When a head
location is rolled against a hydra, roll
again to see which specific head is struck.

The statistics provided beow are for a
default two headed hydra, the most basic form.
For each head beyond the second, the hydra
gains the following bonuses: STR +1, GON
+1, SIZ +3, and +1 Armour Point. Thus an
average seven headed hydra is a terrible
monster, gaining +5 STR, +5 CON, +15 =
SIZ and +5 AP in addition to its base

+ Characteristics

HYENA

Gloranthan Hyenas aresavage canine creatures with pow-
erful jaws, akin to their earth analogue but bigger In Gen-
ertela, they live in Prax, the Wastes and Pent; whilst unusual
packs of all-white or shaggy hyenas can also be found in the
Pamaltelan lands of Jolar and Kothar respectively Hyenas
are capable runners and normally hunt at night, but are
opportunistic scavengers. A ‘cackle” of hyenas can often be
found following a few miles behind any nomadic clan.

In combat, hyenas attack as a pack, chasing prey until it
becomes exhausted, then circling just out of reach. One indi-
vidual at a time then leaps forwards to snap at the target,
whilst covering the evading retreat of the previous attacker.
‘They usually aim for the legs, hobbling prey in place, where:
they can be worn down. Other than Select Location, they
also use Grip to worry at the wound, inflicting automatic

IMPALA JACK O'BEAR

Fourth of the herd beasts of Prax, impala are small ante-
lope usually found ridden by the pigmies of the Impala Tribe.
‘Unassuming and pacifistic by nature, they are famed for their
ability to spring high into the ai, bounding over obstacles
such as man-high walls, or twice that if unburdened. Since
they eat brown, dry grasses, impala thrive across Prax and
the Wastes, being the most numerous of the grazing animals,

Unlike the other herd beasts, impala have no effective
offensive capability; relying instead on their consummate
facility to prance back and forth to escape predators. Due
to this innate ability they can automatically disengage (and
never end up prone) when evading in combat. As mounts,
they are often trained to leap atop foes from beyond engage-
ment range, in order to knock them prone (gee RuNEQuEST
page 152) despite a limited ability to inflict physical damage,
Jn addition, their riders take advantage of these springs to
shoot arrows at the apogee of the leap, making them formi-
dable missile troops.

ro

‘Mostly limited to the regions of Ralios, Froncla and Maniria,
they roam the wilderness preying upon animals and sapient
people. Although only slightly bigger and stronger than an
average man, jack o'bears are greatly feared for theirsly cun-

‘This power seizes physical control over a target, render-
ing them immobile or moving them as a puppet, at the will,
of the carnivorous beast. Each harmonisation attempt takes
a Combat Action to perform (cither proactive or reactive),
and costs a single Magic Point. The target may attempt to
resist in an opposed rolll of their Willpower against the jack
o’bear’s Harmonise skill. Success allows the victim to con-
nue unhindered.

‘The maximum number of targets which ajack o’bear can
harmonise at any one time is equal to half its POW. Fright-
eningly, the duration of the effectdasts until the monster or
victim's death, or, until the magic of the curse is dismissed
using a spell witha Magnitude greater than one tenth of the
jacko'bear’s Willpower.

JOLANTI

Living humanoid stone statues fashioned by the Mostali,
jolanti are used as general labourcrs on tasks consummate to
their large size. As artifidal constructs they do not reproduce,
but must be manufactured via complex magical crafting tech-
niques, almost forgotten by the majority of dwarfs Thus as
they slowly wear down or break, their numbers grow ever less.

_jlantiis a formidable foe; its solid stone bulk not only provide

invulncrable, Any weapon which strikes a jolanti that is not

Karrc BeetLe

Named after the Uz war god for their great strength,
“Karrg Beetles are used as domesticated mounts and pack
beasts. Giant scarabs are dangerous foes due to their tough

of Karrg use them as shod; troops or tide them into combat

NIGHTRIDER

Subversive chaotic monstrosities fiom Pamaltela, night
riders have the appearance of a squat, hunched-over rodent
with jet black skin, red eyes and a flattened skull. They are
rarely encountered unless riding the back of some random
creature, usually an apex predator, massive herbivore or
member of asapient race connected to the back or neck
of the victim with their elongateds root-like fingers and toes
which are used to burrow into their prey.

Besides possessing an unnatural vitality nightriders
can transmit emotions and mental compulsions to their
‘mount’, overcoming its natural instincts or behaviour, Such

Sew ln Om Cr xeomayvyeaod

### Page 174
ADVENTURES IN GLORANTHA ¥ ALL TH WorLD's MONSTERS VY

monstrosity counting as if always using the Brace combat
action (see RUNEQuEsT page 137) but substituting their STR
forSIZ.

Note that a nightrider cannot evade whilst connected to a
victim. Striking at if requires engaging its mount in combat
and use of the Select Target special effect. If their mount is
Iilled a nightrider will detach iself, either fleeing overwhelm-
ing odds, or make an attempt to dominate anew replacement.

amination is ruthless, forcing the victim m perform actions
against their will, from attacking a member of their own fam-
ily to potentially if capable casting magic.

‘Whilst this domination may not be appreciated, the night
rider takes care that its mount is well treated, providing several
symbiotic advantages. Firstly the victim gains the exceptional

~ senses of the nightrider, its Stealth skill and the benefit of its
evil intellect. Secondly, prdviding it is conscious, the night-
rider can transfer Magic Points, Hit Points (to the equivalent
location) and levels of Fatigue between the both of them, to
ensure they remain functional in dangerous stations For
example; a nightrider could transfer all or part of a 6 Hit
Point injury from its own head, to the head of its mount (or
vice versa), potentially reducing a Major to. a Minor Wound.

‘This ability even extends to spells cast at, or by, the night-
sider or its mount, being able to shift them back and forth
according to what is most beneficial. Thus a Demoralise suc-
cessfully cast upon the diabolical creature can be transferred
to the mount instead. Magic transference can be performed
as.a Free Action once per Turn.

A nightrider can voluntarily remove its mot-like digits in
order to change to a more suitable mount, taking one full a
Round to complete. Ripping it free using Brawn is usually
folly, since physical contact (even through armour) places the
attacker under the domination of the nightrider. Attempting
to knock one off its mount however is a different matter; the

NIGHTSTALKER

Painfully thin and gangling humanoid giants of barely
sapient nature, nightstalkers roam the northern jungles of
Pamaltela hunting anything foolish cnough to cross their
path. Standing up to four metres tall at the shoulder, their
beads droop at the end of elongated, wrinkly necks. Skin is a
pasty grey colour, and each limb ends in a hand with which
they can brachiate through the mees.

Nocturnal and sometimes cannibalistic, a nightstalker
creeps up on prey using the canopy to avoid detection,
and then either dangles down hanging by a foot-hand, or
drops atop unaware targets. Either way it grabs up prey in
its overlarge hands, and on its following Turn, swings them
into the nearest solid object. This inflicts twice its damage
‘bonus upon the poor victim, assuming they have a SIZ no
greater than half the nightstalker’s STR. After the prey has
‘been broken, the nightstalker generallyretreats to enjoy their
bloody meal in peace.

tidors to hammering bronze. Since they are not truly living
beings, they work on tirelestly even if worn to the point of
failure, Each is given a crude humanoid form purposed for

NymMPH

Nymphs are guardian spirits of natural featuresorplacesof
outstanding serenity, such as high mountain valleys, tranquil
pools or forest groves. Normally residing on the Spirit Plane,
they occasionally manifest themselves as lithe females — of
either hideous countenance or unearthly beauty —sometimes

OCurnt tas @tArzeree ek 187

to sport with the inhabitant of their realms, otherwise to aid
or warn off mortals

‘As spirits they lack the ability to discerporate or otherwise
attack mortals in Spirit Combat. Yet they have other pow-
ers with which they can protect and control their homes
Nymphs usually have a Spisit Intensity of 1d3+2, although
stronger ones are more often worshipped as local deities.

‘The physical manifestation of a nymph costs it | Magic
Point. The body forms from the natural substance of their
sacred home; thus a dryad might seem to step out of the
trunk of a tree, whilst a hag would weave itself outof the mist
and shadows. Likewise when 4 nyanph abandons their physi-
cal shape they mustretreat back to the trees, shadows, waters
or rocks from which they were formed. Using this ability a
nymph can lure and trick trespassers by seemingly stepping
magically from once plare to another. However, a nymph is
spiritually tied to their home and cannot range more than
their POWx10 metres beyond its farthest extent.

Attacking and destroying the physical manifestation of
a nymph has no effect on their spirimal exence, although
it may greatly anger the entity. There are only two ways to
truly harm a nymph. The first requires travelling onto the
Spirit Plane and defeating them in Spirit Combat. Reducng

OsTRICH

Another of the lesser tribal mounts of Prax, the ostrich is
famed for its obnoxious personality and the ability to outrun
any other Praxian beast: At a run it can achieve incredible
speeds, but the bird is unable to maintain the gait for more
than a short period if carrying a rider. However, utilising
the speed as skirmish troops enables ostrich riders to pepper
slower moving troops with near impumity.

Despite looking rather ridiculous, ostriches are remarkably
dangerous in. close combat. Their clawed feet are capable of
disembowelling 4 full grown man, and the birds tend ip leap

Glorantha is filled with birds of prey, Manirian Eagles,
‘Vrok Hawks and Valtures to name a few. Although excep-

certain divine and spirit cults, most are found in the wild
leading the life of un-extraordinary animals. As the sky chik
dren of Vrimak and Avarnia, all raptors have wings, beaks
and claws; can ly and possess excellent eyesight.

Raptors are generally ineffective combatants against
armoured opponents, save perhapsas distractions or snatch-
ing away weapons, whilst they themselves are hard to strike

Raptor, GIANT

rantha, the most infamous of which are perhaps the Great
‘Hawks of Balazar and the King Condors of the Barder-
lands. Despite their vastly different plumages, these immense
birds are all brothers, akin in size, ‘strength and endurance,
and are able to bear the weight of aman whilst flying Thus
these creatures are most often encountered in the role of
batde mounts.

RUNNER

Minor Aldryami spirits given body in bushes and shrubs,
yunners can take a myriad of different farms, from multi-
branched tumbleweeds to undulating vines. Some can even
take a rough humanoid shape, looking akin to crude topi-
ary, almost undetectable against other woodland or jungle
vegetation provided it remains still. They often co-opt local
animals to provide more rapid means of tansportation if
they are urgently required elsewhere.

Although runners usually lack courage and full intel-
ligence, they make excellent skirmishers for harassing and
distracting foes. Depending on the subspecies they can be
modestly effective in cither close combat or at range, espe-
cially if trespassers are unaware of their presence. They are
normally armed with armed with thorns (Lmpale), nuns (Stun
Location) or whip-like tendrils (Trip or Entangle), Possessing
so many different physiologies, runners are given generic Hit
‘Locations which can be described as needed. For case of
bookkeeping, it is often better to treat runners as Rabble (see
RuweQuesr page 164).

SABLE

Fifth and last of the great herd beasts of Prax, sable are
very large antelope armed with magnificent backwards cur
ing, spiral horns Although smaller than ponies, they arc
strong enough to beara lightly armed rider. Named for their
black colouring, sables are able to eatany of the varied vege-

other beasts by their rather aggressive behaviour.

Sables are quite willing to standoff against threats, utilis-

the horns cannot impale, butare capable of knocking human

SLiMe DEER

‘Slime deer are the cursed perversion of Chaos, the resultof
the Deer God falling during the Great Darkness. Also known
as Gray Dees, due to the colour of their fur, they mainly roam
the wilds of Slontos, but can be found farther afield. Physi-
cally they have the body and legs of a normal deer, the head
however’is a horrific sack of skin which, lacking bones or
muscle, dangles sickeningly between their forelegs.

‘They feed by vomiting acidic digestive juices over plants,
then sucking up the putrid mess ance the vegetation has lig-
uefied. Few creatures willingly hunt slime deer due to the
meat’s Chaotic taint and foul mste. Nevertheless, if assaulted
and unable to flee, the creature will vomit over its attackers
in self defence. Damaging the head sack does not affect the
slime deer unduly, although once the location has received a
Major Wound, the creature is rendered senseless (blind, deaf
and no sense of smell). Some slime deer are so infused with
Chaos they also have a | in $ chance of a Chaos Feature.

VENOMOUS SNAKES

‘There are countless types of vipers spread acsoss all the
continents of Glorantha. They range from one to three
metres in length. Although their mouths are universally too
small to damage humanoids, their venom is not to be under-
estimated. Vipers should be treated more akin to anc-shot
traps or accidental encounters, biting out of selfdefence
before wriggling away or being hacked down by the victim.

‘Treat an average viper as having a Stealth skill of
70+1d 10%, and a Toxic Strike combat style of 60+1d10%.
By default they possess the Cold-Blooded and Venomous
abilities, and use Inject Venom if they win a special effect
in combat. Each species has its own venom as defined in the

SPIDER

‘There are several types of spiders in Glorantha, most of
those found in the wild are individuals which hunt creatures |
up to their own size. However some species of spider are
more socially organised. Those of Dorastor live as coopera-
tive colonies, consisting of smaller male hunters and larger
egg-laying females, under the ruling guidance of a Great
Mother. On the other hand, non-sapient giant spiders can
be found as domesticated riding and pack beasts across Glo-
rantha, wherever there is an Uz tribe.

Due to their morphology, the loss of legs does not inca
pacitatea spider. For guidance ing websand venom,
refer to the rules as described for Giant Spiders (see Rune-
Quest page 388). Use the Giant Spider characteristics for
‘Troll riding and pack spiders, save that the Potency of their

Sea Tn Onreomeg Vso

### Page 190
venom is half the standard value and their DEX is only
2d6+6; being bred for load bearing rather than as predators.

DonesticateD SPAWN

Large numbers of small (3-10cm diameter) unintelligent
spiders which are similar in nature and behaviour to ants.
Male hunters control domesticated spawn with scent markers
for use by the female breeders, who perceive spider spawns
asa food source, a passive territorial defence, and a managed
art form when incorporated into their web sculptures Treat
as per an Insect Swarm (RUNEQUEST page 365).

Mate HUNTER

These short-lived spiders are the smallest of the trie giant
species, with limited, instinctive intelligence. They perform
the menial tasks of a spider dan as hunters, herders, scaven-
gers and labourers, their behaviour hardwired from hatch-
ing and controlled by scent commands from female breed
ers. Scarily fast and agile, male hunter spiders rarely grow to
more than metre long from fang to spinneret.

‘When threatened, male hunters become aggressive and
coordinate with pack tactics, such as distracting with fion-
tal attacks while deploying from flanks or above, or driving
prey into web traps. They tend to use grappling or the Grip
special eflect to immobilise a limb, allowing fellow spiders to
gang up on the hindered foe. When facing superior numbers,
their tattics change to those of hit and run from ambush,
attempting t inject venom on a lucky bite, or stealthily use
their sticky silk as Bshing lirtes from above to try and disarm
enemies or jerk them up intothick foliage, where they dangle
helplessly.

FeMALE BREEDER

Larger than their male servitors with a body length of
several metres, female breeder: live for well over a century,
doing little more than laying enough eggs for maintaining the
colony, Although truly sapient, their intelligence is difficult
to assess except by action, as they only communicate using
pheromone laden scents. Due to greater size, breeders are
typically dower when moving and dislike engaging’in fights,
relying on male hunters to bring food and protect them.

If faring combat, female breeders scuttle deeper into their
warrens, drawing foes into pre-prepared traps; for instance
sticky webs or deep pits disguised by a thin layer of dirt cov-
ered webbing. They alsocast magic in support of male hunter
packs. In those cases where the breeder can no longer flee,
the spider will find anarrow space where onlya single foe can
face them, then pinion the enemy with one of their forelegs
before biting and injecting the typical paralytic spider venom.
Once immediate danger has passed, victims are wrapped in
silk and either offered asa hostage to cease the assault upon
their nest, or kept as food for freshly hatched spiderlings

Great MoTHER

The biggest spiders in Glorantha; the bloated, swollen
body of a great mother can be as much as four metres in
length. Sporting such a mass, they rarely move from their
webs atthe centre of a spider colony — instead relying on the
female breeders to attend them. Each great mother acts as
the orade and teacher for their colony, educating in the arts
of magic whilt giving guidance when asked for.

Despite their natural size and strength, great mothers
never lower themselves to combat, as the entire colony will
sacrifice itself to protect her, She will have already lost all
her ‘children’ by the time she & directly threatened, so the

Ourkt tH. @TArAoekR JOD

some major piece of spider enlightenment, sadly Jost upon
those who cannotcomprehend pheromone communication,
then call upon the Great Ancient Mother, vanishing forever
from the world, Anyone involved in the ‘death’ of a great
mother must win an opposed roll of each Rune Affinity they
possess against her Devotion skill, otherwise be permanently
severed from that Rune ~ a curse which can only be reversed
by an epic Heroquest of pious atonement to Arachne Solara

UNICORN

Unicorns are white, horse-like creatures which live in the
forests of Glorantha and the plains of Prax. Famed for their
grace and long horn, unicorns also possess tasselled tails and
a goatlike beard. They differ from many other beasts by
being fullly sapient, and are able to comprehend language,
despite being unable to speak themselves. This does not pre-
clude them from expressing themselves via body language
however.

Although they appear to be simple equines, unicorns are
highly magical and are universally male, requiring a virgin
female of a lewer species of quadruped, such as amare, does
or even legendarily human females, in order to reproduce.
Mating is arare event, however, as unicorns are believed to
be near immortal and unable to die except via violent acts.

‘Most unicorns are capable of casting Falk Magic despite
their lack of speech. In addition to storing Magic Points, the
hor of a unicorn can also heal injuries at a cost of 1 Magic
Point per Damage Point, no matter how severe the wound.
Similarly they can exorcise diseases at a cost in Magic Points
equal to the Intensity of the Sickness Spirit, dissipating the

Life Serse, Night Sight, Poison.

VAMPIRE

‘The so called ‘nobility’ of Gloranthan undead, vampires:
are those who have undertaken the Rite of Vivamort to irre-
-versibly sunder themselves from the Death Rune; exchang-
ing the cycle of rebirth for an eternal existence as a spirit
bound to their own, no-otiger living corpse.

‘Severed from death, but not alive, a vampire is an
accursed creature forced to drain lfe-foree from others in
order to continue their own existence. Vampires are never
able to slake the continual thirst which torments them, as
they themselves are bound directly to Vivamort, who drains
their stolen life to maintain his own continuaton. In effect
they are but parasites, who in turn are parssitically preyed
upon by their lord, ‘gifting’ them entropic powers in return.

Gloranthan vampires have no need to feed on blood,
nor do they gain sharp fangs and claws, although nothing
stops them from filing their own teeth. Indeed, other than
Magic Points they require no sustenance at all. On the other”
hand vampires are subject to the terrible curses placed upon
‘Vivamort during the Gods Time; by the Styx, for breaking
his oath to stand etemal guard over the Ternble Sccret, by
‘Yelm, who burned and drove Vivamort from Hell for allow-
ingdeath to be brought to thesurface world; and by Ty Kora
‘Tek, for stealing the souls which were hers.

‘The strengths of a Gloranthan vampire are:

& A vampire ceases to age, granting them vast amounts:
‘of time to develop many skills and other interests.

% A vampire gains the Undead creature ability, render-
ing itimmuneto the detrimental effects of injuries and
Fatigue. Upon receiving a Major Wound the vampire
merely turns into smoke and begins to regenerate

‘The only exceptions to this is if the Major Wound is
an Impale to the heart (Chest) which transfixes them
for as long as the weapon remains in place, preventing
the vampire from turning into smoke; or decapitation
which destroys them.

®& A yampire is immune to the effect of poisons and
disease.

®% A vampire’s Characteristic STR is doubled.

& A vampire gains the ability to steal 1d3 Magic Points
from a victim by touching them. This works
through armour (though not parrying weapons or
shields), and allows the vampire to recharge their own
‘Magic Points up to the limit set by their Characteris-

lost. This ability also works in Spirit Combat, Dissipat-

& A vampire who drains a practitioner of theism to zero
‘Magic Points caninstead steal 1d3 points from the vic~

‘the vampirecasts the stolenspells, however the vampire

@ A vampire ako gains a Gaze Attack, essentially immo-
Lilsing a person who meets their eyes, if they fail to
‘overcome the vampire in an opposed test of Willpower

fo expend an Action Point and costs them 1 Magic
Point.

‘Whereas the weaknesses of a vampire are:

& Vampires are forever bound to their god Vivamort,
who feeds upon them to prevent his own annihilation.
At the end of cach night a vampire loses 1 Magic Point
automatically If thisreduces them to zero they fall inert
and utterly helpless, unable w continue their existence
until fed by some underfing usually in the form of a
blood sacrifice.

% The source of their fall and path t etemal annihila-
tion, vampires greatly fear the Death Rune. They suf
fer a penahy of Formidable when trying to resist any
magic drawing upon it, and its effects will be doubled

if applicable. For example a Death Rune-powered Dis-
ruption spell inflicts 243 damage, rather than just 143.
® Vampires are cursed by the River Styx. A single drop
its waters will instantly destroy any vampire it touches.
In deference to breaking the cath sworn on her waters,
all the other rivers of Glorantha will inflict 1d6 dam-
age per round on a vampire, to each Hit Location
immersed in their running waters. This damage can
never be regenerated, ultimately resulting in the vam-
pire being dissolved away as if in concentrated acid.

A vampire suffers fram the direct light of Yelm. When
bathed in hisrays,a vampire loses the overt supernatu-
ral powers of its magic draining touch, immobilising
gaze and ability to transform into a cloud of smoke
the latter permitting the vampire to be killed although
it will rise again next Freezeday night if not otherwise
decapitated, burned or immersed in running water. In
addition, fire magic drawn from the Sky Rune auto-
matically inflicts maximum damage against a vampire
if it fails to resist, the burns not regenerating until the
next Vivamort Holy Day.

2 Vampires are cursed by Ty Kora Tek fior desecrating
the sanctity of the tomb (their own and others). Vam-
pires are forever bound to the place of their creation,
unable to travel further than their POW in kilometres
from the sail, tomb or alter where they were made. Any
further and the earth saps their Magic Points at a rate
of 1 per hour Some vampires try to circumvent this
curse by transporting the rock or soil of their genesis
wholesale to a new location, leaving them vulnerable if
the material is ever found and scattered.

& ompires in their smoke form are unable to coalesce
in windy conditions, being tempomrily dispersed for 2
number of hours equal to one tenth of the STR of
the ambient wind or syiph blowing it. Adopting smoke
form whilst completely submerged in running water
immediately destroys the vampire.

Although almest any sapient creatureis capable of becom
ing a vampire, mest are human in origin due to the ault’s
predominance in the lands once controlled by Gbaji and his
infamous Vampire Legion. When creating a vampire, dou-
ble its Characteristic STH and add the following Creature
Abilities: Allergy (Running Water), Disease Immunity, Gaze
Attack (Mesmerism), Immortal, Magic Drain (Magic Points,
Rune Spell), Poison Immunity, Regeneration (IHP/Round
as Smoke), Undead, Weakness (Death Rune magic, Sky/Fire
Rune magic, Sunlight).

WALKTAPUS

One of the most feared Chaos creaturesever to emerge in
the Greater Darkness, walktapi possess manlike: bodies with
heads similar to a giant octopus By preference they live in
dank wet places such as swamps or stagnant pook, and being
amphibious have the ability to breathe both air and water,
They utilise this capability to submerge and ambush prey
which passes nearby, dragging them away under the cover of
an obscuring cloud of poison gas similar to the effect of an
‘octopus squirting ink (see Walktapus Poison Cloud).

POISON CLO

In combat a walktapus may attack with any ar all of its
eight slimy tentacles which latch on, constricting the Hit
Location struck against which armour only protects until
ity Armour Points are overcome, They use their Grappler
ability to render the weapons or arms of attackers useless,
setting them up for a second tentacle attack that, if suc-
cessful, will begin to tear the victim asunder Rending still
requires the walktapus to spend an Action Point and roll
its attack, but the victim may resist using their Brawn skill

(with appmpriate penalties due to differences in Damage
Modifier). If the rending attack is not resisted, it automati-
cally inflicts damage to one of the Hit Locations
grappled, ignoring any armour usually
resultingin an appendage being torn out

torso, torn in half!

less than hoped for, and the newly created wymms rapidly

magic. Water wyrms on the other hand, live in the seas and
rivers of Glorantha, Their vestigial wings are used as swim-

ZEBRA

Created by a Heroquest by the ancient rulers of Pavis,
the zebra is a sub species of horse whose magical stripes (a
sign of their bondage to Eiritha) sander them from ther
brethren. As a result of this mythic servitude, zebra arc able
to survive on the marginal grazing in Prax and the Wastes,
something normal horses are unable to do.

Most zebras are little more than riding or baggage
+ mounts, their primary defence being that of using their
stripes to remain unobserved fiom a distance, War Zebras
are a nobler breed, able to fight by kicking out with their
hooves, combined with an occasional mouth nip. Although
itde more than a large pony, they are more than a match
for impala or sables. The following statistics represent war
zebra, lesser beasts having three points fewer STR and SIZ.

ADVENTURES IN GLORANTHA & CHARACTERS

100 UNIQUE GLORANTHA BACKGROUND EVENTS

A bag of old bones has been in your family for generations. It is claimed that the bones belong to a great hero of your people. As such the
bones are sacred relics and must always be treated with reverence. Occasionally, your grandmother would set the bones in a line and chant

1 - prayers over them. You always thought she was a bit strange. Then, a few years ago a priest came to your home and demanded to see the

bag of bones. Your grandmother brought them forth and the priest gazed into the bag. He let out a terrified scream, dropped the bag, and
fled from your home. When you looked in there, the bones appeared to be quite normal, Now the bag is in your possession. What caused
the priest to flee? What do the bones aneaDe Who did they belong to? Why do they occasionally rattle of their own accord?

“A female relative i is the most beautiful creature for many, many miles. As the two of you are great friends, you also become the focus of

_ attention from those who desire her. Are you jealous? Are you pleased? Is the attention annoying? Can you make use of it?

A poor traveller came to your village seeking help and shelter. You fed him, clothed him, and tended his wounds. He claimed to be just
a lowly wanderer who had been robbed on the road. The next day, he had gone, taking all your family’s wealth. Recently you attended a
3 feast with lots of rich and important people. There, at the high table, laughing and joking, was the ‘poor’ traveller who robbed you. You

did nothing at the time because you could not be completely certain, but now you are sure it is same man. What will you do? How will you

gain justice for your family? Will anyone. believe you?

A setae ole (oword, armour or jewelry) owned or protected By your family was stolen by enemies. You have sworn to retrieve it from

A prick insisted tht someone aie to you be sacrificed: to ensure a good harvest following several poor and failed harvest years. Although
s) your relative went willingly to the sacrifice, you have not forgotten the screams that followed. The harvest was no better that year. You now
hate all priests and abhor any human sacrifice,

A ieee relative who had embraced the Lunar Way, and was an ardent follower of the’Red Moon Goddess, has suddenly recanted his (or
her) views and embraced another religion with equal fervour. Why is this? Is it a sign that the Lunars have no real power in the world? If
_ you are a Lunar, how do you feel about this sudden conversion?

A sibling has been betrothed to someone from your childhood that you consider an enemy. You are forced to make a sullen peace with this
7 new in-law, but your hatred still burns beneath. What is worse is that you fear your sibling is being turned against you. What can you do to
set matters to rights?

‘A waveller visits your community and demonstrates almost supernatural wisdom. You are fascinated by what you see, but the individual
= does not remain long enough for you to learn more. You do, however, receive dreams that show you meeting up with this person again and
__ learning from him. When, where and how will form a future part of your story.
